Refuting the Question of God's Essential Generosity
Maturidi refutes a question about God's generosity being essential.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the question 'Why is God generous?' is invalid in Maturidi theology because God's attributes are essential and not separable from His essence.

Core Idea
God's attributes are essential, not acquired—asking why is like asking why God is God.

Imam Maturidi addresses a subtle theological question: if God is generous by essence, why does He create? At first glance, the question seems reasonable, but Maturidi reveals a fundamental flaw: it treats God's action as something separate from His essence. In this lesson, we will unpack his concise refutation and see how it preserves divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice how the argument moves from an assumption to a conclusion about the question's invalidity.
The passage is dense; read slowly.
2
Identify the question Maturidi refutes
The implicit question is: 'If God is generous by essence, why does He create?' Maturidi first concedes that one might say creation follows from His generosity.
3
Understand the core objection
Maturidi declares the basis of the question invalid because it equates God's action (creating) with His essence, as if creation were an additional act. But in pre-eternity (al-azal), God is already described by these attributes without any external action.
This is the key point: attributes are not separate from essence.
4
Reflect on the analogy
Maturidi compares asking 'Why is God generous?' to asking 'Why is God Lord?' Both are essential properties—asking for a cause is meaningless. This reinforces the doctrine of tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم جائز أن يقال : إذ هو بذاته جواد ، وبذاته قادر ، وبذاته عالم فجاد تخلقه على خلقه ، إذ هو خلقه إذ هو قادر على أن يجود ويظهر مواهبه . وأصل هذا السؤال عندنا فاسد ؛ لأنه يجعل الفعل هو الذات ، وهو به موصوف في الأزل، والسؤال عن ذلك كالسؤال على أنه لم كان رباً عالما ، ولا قوة إلا بالله .
Then it is permissible to say: Since He is generous by His essence, capable by His essence, and knowing by His essence, then His generosity necessitates His creation, since He is His creation, since He is capable of being generous and manifesting His gifts. And the basis of this question according to us is invalid; because it makes the action identical to the essence, while He is described by it in pre-eternity. And asking about that is like asking why He is Lord and Knowing. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 734

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a hypothetical question about God's attributes. The author states that the question 'why is God generous?' is answered by pointing out that generosity, capability, and knowledge are essential to God's very being. The author then declares the basis of the question invalid because it equates God's action with His essence—as if creation were an additional act separate from His essence—whereas in pre-eternity (al-azal) God is described by these attributes. Asking why He is generous is thus akin to asking why He is Lord or Knowing, which are essential. The passage guards against anthropomorphic or accidental conceptions of divine attributes.

Key Terms
ذات (essence)
جواد (generous)
قادر (capable)
عالم (knowing)
فعل (action)
أزل (pre-eternity)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God's attributes are accidental or acquired, or that God's action of creating is separate from His essence.
Correction: Maturidi affirms that God's attributes are essential and that action does not add anything to His essence. The question wrongly assumes a separation between God's being and His doing.

Checkpoint
What is the basis of the author's refutation of the question about God's generosity?
A) It is impossible to ask about God's actions.
B) The question assumes creation is separate from essence.
C) God's attributes are acquired.
D) The questioners are unbelievers.

Key Takeaway
God's essential attributes are not caused by anything external; asking why they exist is an invalid question that misconstrues the relationship between God's essence and His actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face hardship, do you find yourself questioning God's generosity or wisdom as if He owes you an explanation? How does this lesson challenge that tendency?
?
Think of a time when you demanded to know 'why' from God. In light of this passage, does that demand reflect a view of God as having acquired or caused attributes? What would it look like to trust His essential attributes instead?
?
If God's attributes are essential and uncaused, what does that mean for how you approach Him in worship? Are you willing to stop asking 'why' and simply submit to His described nature, even when you don't understand?

The Maker's Wisdom vs. Naturalists' Self-Management Claim
Maturidi's refutation of naturalists using the fatigue argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Maturidi argues that the order of the universe cannot be due to the self-management of the stars but must come from a wise Maker with knowledge and power.

Core Idea
The universe's order cannot be self-managing; only a wise Maker's knowledge and power can sustain it.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi confronts the naturalists' idea that the celestial bodies manage themselves by their own natures. He argues that such self-management would entail fatigue and pain, which is not observed. Therefore, the perfect order must be the work of a knowing and powerful Maker.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how Maturidi presents the naturalists' claim and his rebuttal.
The text ends abruptly; interpret the argument from the context given.
2
Identify the two opposing views
Find where Maturidi states the naturalists' position (that the Maker's act proceeds from His knowledge and power) and where he contrasts it with the idea of the stars managing themselves.
The naturalists agree on a Maker but attribute order to His knowledge, not to the natures.
3
Understand the fatigue argument
Maturidi argues that if the stars were self-managing, they would suffer fatigue and pain from perpetual motion, just like living beings. Since this is not observed, they are not self-managing.
This is a reductio ad absurdum against the naturalists' implicit claim that stars act by their own agency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم تكلم هؤلاء بما تكلم به أصحاب الطبائع : إن ذلك الصانع " إنما خرج فعله حكما متقنا بما عنده من العلم وله من القدرة، ولولا ذلك لا احتمل ما ذكرت فإنه بما سبق من التدبير استقام ذلك، فمثله أمر النجوم، أو كان على ما يقول / كان يكون ذلك كذلك بتدبير عليم حكيم أنشأه على ذلك. ولو كان إليها التدبير لما يحتمل أن تتعب نفسها بالسير والشركات الدائمة وتؤلمها؛ إذ كذلك حال الأحياء في الشاهد، إن تلك الأحوال تتعبهم وتعلمهم، أو أن يكون من الموات
Then these spoke as the naturalists spoke: That the Maker only produced His act perfectly ordered because of what He possesses of knowledge and power. Were it not for that, it would not be possible what I mentioned, for by the preceding management it became sound. So likewise is the matter of the stars, or as he says: it would be so by the management of a Knowing, Wise One who created it upon that. And if the management were to them [the stars themselves], it would not be possible that they would tire themselves with perpetual motion and partnerships and cause pain to themselves, for such is the case of living beings in the witnessed world: these states tire them and cause them pain, or that they be from the inanimate.
Source pages p. 744

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the naturalists' claim that the order in the universe is due to the inherent natures or the stars themselves. Maturidi argues that the precision of creation points to a Maker with knowledge and power. If the management belonged to the stars, they would not willingly undertake perpetual motions that cause them fatigue and pain, as observed in living beings. Therefore, the order must come from an external wise Creator.

Key Terms
صانع
علم
قدرة
تدبير
حكيم
أحياء
موات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The stars and planets have their own intelligence and manage their motions by themselves without an external cause.
Correction: Maturidi argues that if they had such agency, they would experience fatigue and pain from perpetual motion, which is not observed. Therefore, the management must come from an external wise Creator, not from the stars themselves.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi argue that the stars cannot manage themselves?
A) Because they are too far away
B) Because they would tire and suffer from perpetual motion
C) Because they are inanimate
D) Because they are made of fire

Key Takeaway
The perfect order of the universe is proof of the Maker's knowledge and power, not of self-managing natures.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever attributed the order in your life—your health, your career, your relationships—solely to your own efforts, forgetting that it is Allah's knowledge and power that sustain every detail? Identify one area where you take credit and repent by verbally acknowledging His management right now.
?
The stars tirelessly obey Allah's command without complaint. Do you feel exhausted by your daily responsibilities? How can you transform your attitude from seeing duties as burdens to seeing them as acts of worship that align you with the cosmic obedience to your Lord? Commit one specific habit today.
?
If self-leadership led to fatigue, as Maturidi argues, what does that say about your attempts to manage your own affairs without seeking Allah's guidance? Have you ever tried to 'go it alone' and felt drained as a result? Will you consciously submit your plans to Allah tonight in prayer?

beginner
5 min
God's Actions Are Not for His Own Benefit
Maturidi establishes that creation is for consequences, not for God's benefit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that creation cannot be for God's benefit or for destruction, but for the benefit of creatures.

Core Idea
Everything God does is for us, not for Himself.

Maturidi begins by laying down a logical principle: an action from which the doer gets no benefit is defective. Since God is absolutely self-sufficient, His actions cannot be for His own benefit. He then eliminates destruction as a purpose, leading to the conclusion that creation is for consequences that benefit creatures.

Guided Path
1
Read the principle
Read the opening sentence about the defectiveness of an action that brings no benefit to its doer. Reflect on how this applies to God.
Maturidi is using rational argument, not quoting scripture.
2
Eliminate wrong purposes
Notice how Maturidi rules out both self-benefit and destruction as purposes of creation. What logical steps does he use?
3
Identify the correct purpose
Find the sentence where Maturidi states that creation is 'for consequences' and summarize what that means.
The term 'al-'awaqib' refers to outcomes that benefit creatures.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ رحمه الله : ثم الأصل أن من يفعل فعلا لا ينتفع هو به لهلاكه وفنائه أنه عائب ، والله سبحانه لم يكن لينتفع بما ينشئه لتعاليه عن الحاجات وغناه بنفسه عن غيره ، فيبطل أن يكون فعله لينتفع به هو ، ثم لو كان للهلاك لا غير لكان لا معنى لخلقه ، فثبت أن خلق العالم للعواقب ، ثم خلق خلائق لم يجعل عندها تمييزا ولا إدراكا لعواقب الأمر ، ثبت / أنه خلقهم لا لأنفسهم ، وخلق خلقا يعرفون ذلك ويطلبون جميع صنيعهم نفع العواقب حتى من خرج ذلك ؛ إذ هو محتاج كل غير ، حكيم في فعله ، فلزمت محبتهم المنشئ فيهم من العقول التي يدركون بها العواقب ، ولأنهم لو تركوا وتدبيرهم لم يكونوا يرضون من أنفسهم التقلب فيما لا يؤثر نفعا ولا يعقبه حمدا ، ومن تعاطى منهم مثله فهو سفيه جاهل . وإذا لزم ما ذكرنا لزم فى الحكمة خلق الضار والنافع ، وخلق الجوهر المحتمل للألم واللذة وإنشاء الآلام والملاذ ؛ ليعلموا ما يرغب إليه الأنفس وما تهرب منه ، فيحذرون ويرغبون بمثله فيها امتحنوا به ؛ وليعلموا النفع
The Shaykh (may Allah have mercy on him) said: Then the principle is that whoever does an act from which he himself derives no benefit due to its destruction and annihilation, it is defective. And Allah, exalted, is not such that He would benefit from what He creates, due to His transcendence above needs and His self-sufficiency from others. So it is invalid that His act is for His own benefit. Then, if it were for destruction only, there would be no meaning to His creation. So it is established that the creation of the world is for consequences (al-'awaqib). Then He created creatures without giving them discrimination (tamyiz) or perception of the consequences of affairs; it is established that He created them not for themselves. And He created creatures who know that and seek in all their actions the benefit of consequences, even to the extent that if that is lacking, [they are discontent] because he is in need of every other, wise in his action. So their love is necessitated for the originator in them of the intellects (al-'uqul) by which they perceive consequences. And because if they were left to their own management, they would not be satisfied with themselves to fluctuate in what brings no benefit nor is followed by praise. And whoever among them engages in such is foolish and ignorant. And if what we have mentioned is necessitated, then in wisdom it is necessitated to create the harmful and the beneficial, and to create the substance capable of pain and pleasure, and to create pains and pleasures, so that they may know what souls desire and what they flee from, so that they may be cautious and desire by means of that with which they are tested, and so that they may know the benefit.
Source pages p. 764

Commentary
This passage is a theological explanation of the purpose of creation. The author (referred to as al-Shaykh) establishes that God's actions are not for His own benefit because He is transcendent and self-sufficient. Creation cannot be for destruction, so it must be for consequences (benefits for creatures). He distinguishes between creatures without intellect (who are not ends in themselves) and those with intellect, who can perceive consequences. The latter seek benefit in their actions. This necessitates the creation of good and evil, pleasure and pain, as means for humans to choose and be tested. Wisdom requires opposites so that humans may know what to seek and avoid.

Key Terms
عواقب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God creates for His own benefit or for mere amusement.
Correction: Maturidi argues that God is above need, so creation cannot benefit Him, and destruction is meaningless; creation must have a purpose benefiting creatures.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why is it invalid that God's act of creation is for His own benefit?
A) Because God is too great to need benefit
B) Because Allah is transcendent and self-sufficient
C) Because benefit would imply imperfection
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
Creation is not for God's benefit or for destruction, but for the benefit of creatures as consequences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a trial, do you truly believe it has a purpose for your ultimate benefit, or do you see it as random suffering? How does this passage challenge you to change your perspective today?
?
If God does not benefit from your worship, then for whom is your worship actually for? Does this realization change the sincerity of your intentions in prayer and obedience? What one step will you take this week to worship more purely for your own spiritual consequence?
?
The passage rejects the idea that creation is for destruction. Reflect on your own life: are there habits or relationships that are leading you toward spiritual destruction without purpose? What will you do to realign them toward beneficial consequences?

intermediate
6 min
The Role of Intellect in Seeking Benefit
Maturidi distinguishes between intellectless and intelligent creatures, emphasizing the role of intellect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi distinguishes between creatures with and without intellect, and how intellect enables humans to seek beneficial consequences.

Core Idea
Intellect is the tool to perceive consequences and seek benefit.

After establishing that creation is for consequences, Maturidi explains that some creatures lack intellect and are not ends in themselves, while others possess intellect to perceive outcomes. This leads to love for the Creator who gave intellect and condemnation of pointless actions.

Guided Path
1
Contrast two types of creatures
Read the part where Maturidi mentions creatures without discrimination/intellect and those with it. What is the difference in their purpose?
Those without intellect are created not for themselves; those with intellect are responsible.
2
Understand the function of intellect
Intellect enables perception of consequences (al-'awaqib). How does this lead to seeking benefit in actions?
3
Reflect on the love of the Creator
Maturidi says this necessitates love for the Originator of intellect. Why?
Because intellect is a great gift that allows us to choose beneficial actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ رحمه الله : ثم الأصل أن من يفعل فعلا لا ينتفع هو به لهلاكه وفنائه أنه عائب ، والله سبحانه لم يكن لينتفع بما ينشئه لتعاليه عن الحاجات وغناه بنفسه عن غيره ، فيبطل أن يكون فعله لينتفع به هو ، ثم لو كان للهلاك لا غير لكان لا معنى لخلقه ، فثبت أن خلق العالم للعواقب ، ثم خلق خلائق لم يجعل عندها تمييزا ولا إدراكا لعواقب الأمر ، ثبت / أنه خلقهم لا لأنفسهم ، وخلق خلقا يعرفون ذلك ويطلبون جميع صنيعهم نفع العواقب حتى من خرج ذلك ؛ إذ هو محتاج كل غير ، حكيم في فعله ، فلزمت محبتهم المنشئ فيهم من العقول التي يدركون بها العواقب ، ولأنهم لو تركوا وتدبيرهم لم يكونوا يرضون من أنفسهم التقلب فيما لا يؤثر نفعا ولا يعقبه حمدا ، ومن تعاطى منهم مثله فهو سفيه جاهل . وإذا لزم ما ذكرنا لزم فى الحكمة خلق الضار والنافع ، وخلق الجوهر المحتمل للألم واللذة وإنشاء الآلام والملاذ ؛ ليعلموا ما يرغب إليه الأنفس وما تهرب منه ، فيحذرون ويرغبون بمثله فيها امتحنوا به ؛ وليعلموا النفع
The Shaykh (may Allah have mercy on him) said: Then the principle is that whoever does an act from which he himself derives no benefit due to its destruction and annihilation, it is defective. And Allah, exalted, is not such that He would benefit from what He creates, due to His transcendence above needs and His self-sufficiency from others. So it is invalid that His act is for His own benefit. Then, if it were for destruction only, there would be no meaning to His creation. So it is established that the creation of the world is for consequences (al-'awaqib). Then He created creatures without giving them discrimination (tamyiz) or perception of the consequences of affairs; it is established that He created them not for themselves. And He created creatures who know that and seek in all their actions the benefit of consequences, even to the extent that if that is lacking, [they are discontent] because he is in need of every other, wise in his action. So their love is necessitated for the originator in them of the intellects (al-'uqul) by which they perceive consequences. And because if they were left to their own management, they would not be satisfied with themselves to fluctuate in what brings no benefit nor is followed by praise. And whoever among them engages in such is foolish and ignorant. And if what we have mentioned is necessitated, then in wisdom it is necessitated to create the harmful and the beneficial, and to create the substance capable of pain and pleasure, and to create pains and pleasures, so that they may know what souls desire and what they flee from, so that they may be cautious and desire by means of that with which they are tested, and so that they may know the benefit.
Source pages p. 764

Commentary
This passage is a theological explanation of the purpose of creation. The author (referred to as al-Shaykh) establishes that God's actions are not for His own benefit because He is transcendent and self-sufficient. Creation cannot be for destruction, so it must be for consequences (benefits for creatures). He distinguishes between creatures without intellect (who are not ends in themselves) and those with intellect, who can perceive consequences. The latter seek benefit in their actions. This necessitates the creation of good and evil, pleasure and pain, as means for humans to choose and be tested. Wisdom requires opposites so that humans may know what to seek and avoid.

Key Terms
تمييز
عقول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi say that creatures with intellect are necessitated to love the Originator?
A) Because they receive benefits from Him
B) Because He created intellect in them to perceive consequences
C) Because they are forced by nature
D) Because they seek praise

Key Takeaway
Intellect enables humans to perceive consequences, seek benefit, and love the Creator for this gift.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you using your intellect to perceive the ultimate consequences of your actions, or are you living for immediate gratification? What specific decision today requires you to think beyond the moment?
?
If you truly love the Creator for giving you intellect, does your life reflect that love by seeking what is truly beneficial in His sight? Name one area where you are settling for less than that.
?
When you engage in actions that bring no real benefit or lasting praise, do you humbly admit your foolishness, or do you rationalize it? What would it take for you to stop one such habit today?

The Wisdom of Creating Good, Evil, Pain, and Pleasure
Maturidi shows that wisdom demands creation of good/evil, pain/pleasure for testing and knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that divine wisdom requires the creation of opposites like good and evil, pain and pleasure, for human testing and knowledge.

Core Idea
Opposites in creation are necessary for humans to choose and know benefit.

Maturidi concludes his argument by asserting that wisdom necessitates the creation of harmful and beneficial things, as well as the capacity for pain and pleasure. These opposites serve as a means for humans to learn what to seek and avoid, forming the basis of moral testing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conclusion
Read the sentence that begins with 'وإذا لزم ما ذكرنا' (And if what we mentioned is necessitated). What follows?
2
List the created opposites
What are the pairs of opposites Maturidi mentions? (harmful/beneficial, pain/pleasure)
3
Understand the purpose
Why are these opposites created? Look for the phrases 'ليعلموا' (so that they may know) and 'امتحنوا به' (with which they are tested).

God Creates Both Good and Evil
Maturidi affirms God's sole creation of all good and evil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi position that God is the creator of all good and evil, and the theological necessity of this belief to avoid shirk.

Core Idea
God alone creates everything, even the substance of evil.

Maturidi begins by stating his school's core doctrine: Allah is the creator of both good and evil in their very substance, and also creates human actions. This is not a compromise but a direct affirmation of divine omnipotence, coupled with a rejection of any partner in His dominion.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Notice the strong affirmation and the negative statement about partners.
2
Identify the affirmation
Identify the key claims: God creates substance of good and evil, and creates human actions.
3
Understand the negation
Notice the conditional: if anything in His dominion were not created by Him, that would imply a partner. This is a logical argument.
4
Reflect on divine transcendence
Reflect on how this doctrine preserves God's sole sovereignty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما عندنا فنحن نقول بأن الله جل جلاله خالق جوهر الشر والخير وخالق فعل الخلق شرا أو خيرا، ولا يجوز كون شيء في سلطانه لم يخلفه، فيكون له شريك في سلطانه وعديل في خلق عالمه، جل الله عن ذلك وتعالى. ونقول بأن خلق الخلق ليس هو ذلك الخلق، وكذلك فعله، ولا يوصف فعله بالشر والخير، ولا يوصف بأن فعله خير وشر؛ لأنه موصوف يفعله، ولم يقل هو خير ولا شرير، ومن فعله ذلك في الحقيقة فهو مسمى به، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وما يجب في الحكمة خلق الجواهر المؤذية والمناظر القبيحة وخلق الآفات في الحواس أن البشر كلهم قد اعتقدوا شيئا غاب عن حواسهم، إما نفي أو إثبات: منهم من دانوا، ومنهم من تجاهل وحصل على الشهوات، فإذا لم يخلق فيما يقع على الحواس ما ذكرنا لم يعرفوا القبح من الحسن ولا المؤذي من النافع، وإذا لم يعقلوا ذلك لم يحتمل عقولهم درك القبيح من الحسن ولا المؤذي من الملذ، فخلق كذلك ليمثلوا بما تقع عليه الحواس ما لا تقع عليه؛ ليصير كل معتقد غاب عن البصر على ما عليه معروفا بما يشاهده، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And as for us, we say that Allah, exalted be His majesty, is the creator of the substance of evil and good, and the creator of the act of the creation as evil or good. It is not permissible that anything in His dominion be not created by Him, for that would give Him a partner in His dominion and a rival in creating His universe. Allah is far above that and exalted. And we say that the creation of the creation is not that creation, and similarly His act is not that act. His act is not described as evil or good, nor is it said that His act is good or evil; because He is described as doing it, and He is not called good or evil. And whoever does that in reality is called by it. And there is no power except with Allah. And what is necessary in wisdom regarding the creation of harmful substances, ugly scenes, and defects in the senses is that all humans have believed in something absent from their senses, either negation or affirmation: some of them have religion, some are ignorant and follow desires. So if He had not created in what falls upon the senses what we mentioned, they would not know the ugly from the beautiful nor the harmful from the beneficial. And if they do not understand that, their minds cannot comprehend the ugly from the beautiful nor the harmful from the pleasurable. So He created thus so that they may analogize by what falls upon the senses to what does not fall upon them; so that every belief absent from sight becomes known as it is by what is witnessed. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 769

Commentary
This passage presents the core Maturidi doctrine on the problem of evil. First, it affirms that God is the creator of both the substance of evil (e.g., harmful objects) and good, as well as of human actions—whether evil or good. Nothing in God's dominion exists without His creation, otherwise that would imply a partner. Then it makes a distinction: God's act of creating is not the same as the created act (i.e., human actions are not identified with God's act). God's act is not described as evil or good because He is the doer, not the one done to; He is not called evil. Only the one who actually does the act (the human) is called by its name. This preserves divine transcendence. Then Maturidi explains the wisdom behind creating harmful things, ugly scenes, and sensory defects: humans need sensory experience to discern good from evil, harmful from beneficial. These physical experiences serve as analogies for unseen beliefs, helping humans understand abstract truths by analogy with sensory perceptions. Thus, the existence of apparent evils is pedagogically necessary.

Key Terms
خالق جوهر الشر والخير
شريك
سلطان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that attributing creation of evil to God makes Him responsible for sin.
Correction: Maturidi distinguishes between creating the substance and committing the act; God creates the potential, but the human chooses and performs the act.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what would it imply if something in Allah's dominion were not created by Him?
A) That Allah is weak
B) That there is a partner in His dominion
C) That evil is not real
D) That good and evil are illusions

Key Takeaway
God's absolute sovereignty requires that He alone creates all that exists, including the substance of evil and good.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience suffering or witness evil, do you truly believe that even its substance is from Allah, or does your heart incline to resentment? How would your patience change if you accepted this fully?
?
If God creates even the evil inclinations within your own soul, how does that shape your repentance? Will you continue to blame yourself alone, or will you turn to the Creator of all things for transformation?
?
Can you surrender your sense of fairness to the reality that God alone defines good and evil? What would it cost you to release your judgments and submit to His absolute sovereignty?

Distinction Between Creator and Created Act
Maturidi distinguishes God's act of creation from the created act.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi distinction between God's act of creation and the created human act, preserving divine transcendence.

Core Idea
God's act is not described by the moral qualities of the created act.

Maturidi now goes deeper to clarify a subtle point: God's act of creating is not identical with the created act. This distinction prevents attributing evil to God even though He creates evil actions. The passage explains that God is the doer of creation, but His act is not called evil or good; only the human who actually performs the act is described by it.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the passage focusing on the distinction between 'creation of the creation' and 'that creation'.
2
Identify the distinctions
Note two distinctions: 1) The creating is not the created. 2) God's act is not described by the qualities of the created act.
3
Understand the reasoning
Why is God's act not described as good or evil? Because He is the doer of the act of creating, and the doer is not called by the moral quality of the thing done.
This is a key point in Maturidi theodicy.
4
Reflect on human responsibility
Reflect that the passage assigns the moral description to the human who acts, not to God, preserving human free will and accountability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

?

Wisdom Behind the Creation of Harmful Things
Maturidi explains the wisdom behind creating harmful things.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that the existence of harmful substances, ugly scenes, and sensory defects is a necessary part of divine wisdom.

Core Idea
Sensory experiences of harm and ugliness enable humans to discern unseen truths.

Maturidi concludes his discussion on the problem of evil by explaining the wisdom behind the creation of apparent evils such as harmful creatures, ugly sights, and defective senses. He argues that these serve as analogical tools for humans to understand abstract concepts of good and evil, which are necessary for religious belief and moral discernment.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the passage and identify the list of created things: harmful substances, ugly scenes, defects in senses.
2
Understand the argument
Maturidi says that all humans have beliefs about unseen realities. Without sensory experiences of good and evil, they could not discern moral qualities.
This is an epistemological argument.
3
Grasp the analogy
Humans analogize from sensory experiences to unseen realities. So harmful things are necessary for that analogy.
This shows that evil is not pointless.
4
Reflect on divine wisdom
Reflect that this explanation defends God's wisdom in creating a world with apparent evil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما عندنا فنحن نقول بأن الله جل جلاله خالق جوهر الشر والخير وخالق فعل الخلق شرا أو خيرا، ولا يجوز كون شيء في سلطانه لم يخلفه، فيكون له شريك في سلطانه وعديل في خلق عالمه، جل الله عن ذلك وتعالى. ونقول بأن خلق الخلق ليس هو ذلك الخلق، وكذلك فعله، ولا يوصف فعله بالشر والخير، ولا يوصف بأن فعله خير وشر؛ لأنه موصوف يفعله، ولم يقل هو خير ولا شرير، ومن فعله ذلك في الحقيقة فهو مسمى به، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وما يجب في الحكمة خلق الجواهر المؤذية والمناظر القبيحة وخلق الآفات في الحواس أن البشر كلهم قد اعتقدوا شيئا غاب عن حواسهم، إما نفي أو إثبات: منهم من دانوا، ومنهم من تجاهل وحصل على الشهوات، فإذا لم يخلق فيما يقع على الحواس ما ذكرنا لم يعرفوا القبح من الحسن ولا المؤذي من النافع، وإذا لم يعقلوا ذلك لم يحتمل عقولهم درك القبيح من الحسن ولا المؤذي من الملذ، فخلق كذلك ليمثلوا بما تقع عليه الحواس ما لا تقع عليه؛ ليصير كل معتقد غاب عن البصر على ما عليه معروفا بما يشاهده، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And as for us, we say that Allah, exalted be His majesty, is the creator of the substance of evil and good, and the creator of the act of the creation as evil or good. It is not permissible that anything in His dominion be not created by Him, for that would give Him a partner in His dominion and a rival in creating His universe. Allah is far above that and exalted. And we say that the creation of the creation is not that creation, and similarly His act is not that act. His act is not described as evil or good, nor is it said that His act is good or evil; because He is described as doing it, and He is not called good or evil. And whoever does that in reality is called by it. And there is no power except with Allah. And what is necessary in wisdom regarding the creation of harmful substances, ugly scenes, and defects in the senses is that all humans have believed in something absent from their senses, either negation or affirmation: some of them have religion, some are ignorant and follow desires. So if He had not created in what falls upon the senses what we mentioned, they would not know the ugly from the beautiful nor the harmful from the beneficial. And if they do not understand that, their minds cannot comprehend the ugly from the beautiful nor the harmful from the pleasurable. So He created thus so that they may analogize by what falls upon the senses to what does not fall upon them; so that every belief absent from sight becomes known as it is by what is witnessed. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 769

Commentary
This passage presents the core Maturidi doctrine on the problem of evil. First, it affirms that God is the creator of both the substance of evil (e.g., harmful objects) and good, as well as of human actions—whether evil or good. Nothing in God's dominion exists without His creation, otherwise that would imply a partner. Then it makes a distinction: God's act of creating is not the same as the created act (i.e., human actions are not identified with God's act). God's act is not described as evil or good because He is the doer, not the one done to; He is not called evil. Only the one who actually does the act (the human) is called by its name. This preserves divine transcendence. Then Maturidi explains the wisdom behind creating harmful things, ugly scenes, and sensory defects: humans need sensory experience to discern good from evil, harmful from beneficial. These physical experiences serve as analogies for unseen beliefs, helping humans understand abstract truths by analogy with sensory perceptions. Thus, the existence of apparent evils is pedagogically necessary.

Key Terms
حكمة
جواهر مؤذية
مناظر قبيحة
آفات في الحواس
تمثيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The existence of evil in the world proves God is not all-good or all-wise.
Correction: Maturidi argues that apparent evil serves a pedagogical purpose, allowing humans to discern good from evil through sensory analogy, which is necessary for moral and religious understanding.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what would happen if God had not created harmful substances, ugly scenes, and sensory defects?
A) Humans would still know good from evil
B) Humans would not know the ugly from the beautiful nor the harmful from the beneficial
C) Humans would never sin
D) Humans would have perfect knowledge

Key Takeaway
Apparent evils in creation are necessary for humans to understand and analogize to unseen truths, upholding divine wisdom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience something painful or ugly, do you instinctively question Allah's wisdom or complain? How does Maturidi's explanation force you to reconsider that reaction? What specific harm in your life might be a 'sensory example' teaching you about a deeper unseen truth, and are you willing to seek that lesson instead of dwelling on the discomfort?
?
You have believed in unseen realities like Paradise and Hell without seeing them. On what basis do you distinguish between spiritual good and evil? If Allah had not created physical harm and ugliness, would your mind still be able to grasp the concepts of sin and punishment? How does this passage expose your reliance on sensory experiences for faith?
?
The passage says some people follow desires and remain ignorant. When you face a 'ugly' situation, do you immediately turn to your desires or do you pause to analogize and seek wisdom? What would it cost you to practice analogical reasoning (tamthīl) in your next trial instead of reacting impulsively? Commit to one concrete step to implement this today.

God Creates All Actions and Substances – Not Tainted by Evil
Maturidi defends God's sole creative power and His transcendence from evil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi doctrine that God is the sole creator of both good and evil, and why this does not attribute evil to Him.

Core Idea
God creates all, but is not named by His creation; only the doer of an act is named by it.

Maturidi addresses a key concern: if God creates evil, does that make Him evil? He argues that creation is distinct from being the doer, and that terms like 'evil' applied to substances are metaphorical, not real. This distinction safeguards divine transcendence while affirming God's absolute sovereignty.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening objection
Read the first part of the passage where Maturidi presents the view that substances called 'evil' are only metaphorically so. Understand the distinction between literal and metaphorical attribution.
This sets up the problem: if God creates substances that are called evil, how can He be free of evil?
2
Identify the Sunni position
Find the statement beginning with 'As for us, we say...' and note that God is the Creator of both the substance of good and evil and the actions of creatures.
God's creation includes everything in His domain; nothing exists without His creation.
3
Understand the creation-act distinction
Notice that Maturidi distinguishes between God's act of creation and the creature's act. God's act is not described as good or evil; only the doer of the act in reality is named by it.
This preserves God's transcendence: He creates, but is not characterized by what He creates.
4
Reflect on the implication
Ask yourself why this distinction matters for tawhid. How does it prevent associating partners with God?
If anything existed without God's creation, that would imply a partner in His dominion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من الجواهر ، وأنه لم يسم به شريرا ولا مسيئا ، ولا إفساد الأشياء مفسدا ، فكذلك في خلق أفعال الشر والفساد لا يسمى به ، فكان من جوابهم أن الجواهر سميت شرا على المجاز لا على الحقيقة ، وهى فى الحقيقة ليست بالشر . وأما عندنا فنحن نقول بأن الله جل جلاله خالق جوهر الشر والخير وخالق فعل الخلق شرا أو خيرا ، ولا يجوز كون شيء في سلطانه لم يخلفه ، فيكون له شريك في سلطانه وعديل فى خلق عالمه ، جل الله عن ذلك وتعالى . ونقول بأن خلق الخلق ليس هو ذلك الخلق ، وكذلك فعله ، ولا يوصف فعله بالشر والخير ، ولا يوصف بأن فعله خير وشر ؛ لأنه موصوف يفعله ، ولم يقل هو خير ولا شرير ، ومن فعله ذلك فى الحقيقة فهو مسمى به ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . وما يجب في الحكمة خلق الجواهر المؤذية والمناظر القبيحة وخلق الآفات في الحواس أن البشر كلهم قد اعتقدوا شيئا غاب عن حواسهم ، إما نفى أو إثبات : منهم من دانوا ، ومنهم من تجاهل وحصل على الشهوات ، فإذا لم يخلق فيما يقع على الحواس ما ذكرنا لم يعرفوا القبح من الحسن ولا المؤذى من النافع ، وإذا لم يعقلوا ذلك لم يحتمل عقولهم درك القبيح من الحسن ولا المؤذى من الملذ ، فخلق كذلك ليمثلوا بما تقع عليه الحواس ما لا تقع عليه ؛ ليصير كل معتقد غاب عن البصر على ما عليه معروفا بما يشاهده ، ولا قوة إلا بالله .
From the substances, and that He is not called evil or harmful by it, nor is the corruption of things called corrupt, so likewise in the creation of actions of evil and corruption He is not called by it. So from their answer was that the substances are called evil metaphorically, not in reality, and they are in reality not evil. As for us, we say that God, exalted be His majesty, is the Creator of the substance of evil and good, and the Creator of the action of the creature as evil or good, and it is not permissible for anything to exist in His domain that He did not create, for then He would have a partner in His domain and an equal in the creation of His world—glory be to God above that and exalted. And we say that the creation of the creature is not that creature, and likewise His action, and His action is not described as evil or good, nor is it described that His action is good or evil, because He is described by His action, and He is not called good or evil, and whoever does that in reality is named by it, and there is no power except through God. And what is necessary in wisdom—the creation of harmful substances, ugly sights, and the creation of defects in the senses—is that all humans have believed in something absent from their senses, either negation or affirmation: some of them are religious, and some are ignorant and pursue desires. So if He did not create in what falls upon the senses what we mentioned, they would not know ugliness from beauty, nor harmful from beneficial, and if they did not comprehend that, their minds would not bear the perception of the ugly from the beautiful nor the harmful from the pleasant. So He created thus that they might analogize by what falls upon the senses to what does not fall upon them, so that every belief absent from sight becomes known as it is by what is witnessed, and there is no power except through God.
Source pages p. 769

Commentary
This passage is a two-part argument: (1) God is the sole creator of everything, including the substance of good and evil and the actions of creatures, without being tainted by evil, and (2) the wisdom behind creating harmful and ugly things. Maturidi begins by addressing a possible objection: substances called 'evil' are only metaphorically so; in reality they are not. For Sunni Islam, God creates both the substance of good and evil and the actions of creatures, whether good or evil. Nothing exists in His dominion that He did not create, otherwise there would be a partner. The creature's act is distinct from God's act of creation; God's act is not described as good or evil because He is the doer of His own act, and the one who actually performs the act is named by it. The second part explains the wisdom: harmful things are created to allow humans to discern good from evil through sensory experience, which leads to understanding unseen truths. Without such contrasts, people would not recognize ugliness or benefit, and thus could not conceive of the unseen. Therefore, God created these for the purpose of analogy and recognition.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God creates evil, He must be evil or share in evil.
Correction: Maturidi clarifies that creation is not the same as doing. God is not called evil because He creates evil actions; only the one who performs the action is called by that name.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why is God not called evil even though He creates evil actions?
A) Because evil actions are not real
B) Because God's act of creation is distinct from the creature's act, and only the doer of the act is named by it
C) Because God only creates good, and evil comes from something else
D) Because evil is metaphorical and not truly created

Key Takeaway
God creates all actions and substances, including what we call evil, but He is not tainted by evil because creation is distinct from the act performed by the creature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you witness evil in the world, do you ever secretly question God's goodness? How does the distinction between God's creation and the creature's act change the way you view Him? Will you now actively separate the Creator from the created act in your heart?
?
Think of a sin you committed recently. Did you, even for a moment, blame God for giving you the ability to sin? This lesson says only the doer is named by the act. Does your repentance reflect full ownership of that sin? Write a concrete commitment to never shift blame to God again, and to repent sincerely.
?
If God is not tainted by the evil He creates, how should that affect your view of yourself when you do evil? You become 'evil' by your action. Does that sober you into taking greater responsibility for your choices? What specific step will you take today to ensure your actions align with God's good creation?

The Wisdom Behind Harmful Creatures and Defects
Maturidi explains the wisdom behind creating harmful substances, ugly sights, and sensory defects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the wisdom behind God's creation of harmful substances, ugly sights, and defects in the senses according to Maturidi.

Core Idea
Contrast in creation enables humans to recognize good by its opposite and analogize to the unseen.

Maturidi explains that harmful and ugly things are not arbitrary; they serve a crucial purpose. Without them, humans would lack the sensory basis to distinguish good from evil, and thus could not conceptualize unseen realities. This shows God's wisdom in creating a world of opposites.

Guided Path
1
Read the premise
Read the first sentence that states all humans have believed in something absent from the senses, either affirming or denying. Note that this includes both the religious and the ignorant.
This establishes that humans naturally engage with the unseen.
2
Trace the conditional argument
Follow the 'if...then' logic: if God had not created harmful/ugly things, humans would not know ugliness from beauty or harm from benefit. Without that comprehension, they could not grasp the unseen.
Sensory contrasts are necessary for conceptualizing opposites.
3
Understand the purpose
Realize that God created these so that humans can analogize from sensory experiences to unseen realities. By observing physical ugliness, they can conceive of spiritual ugliness (e.g., evil).
This demonstrates divine wisdom and the educational purpose of creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Meaning of Divine Wisdom: Placing Everything in Its Place
Maturidi defines divine wisdom as placing everything in its proper place.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's definition of divine wisdom as the placement of everything in its proper place, independent of human moral judgments on God's acts.

Core Idea
Wisdom is not about moral labels on God's acts, but about placing each thing in its rightful place.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi explains the true meaning of divine wisdom (al-hikma). He argues that God's act of creating different substances, some considered good and some evil, is not to be described by human moral categories; rather, wisdom is about putting everything in its proper context. This sets the foundation for understanding why God creates both beneficial and harmful things.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once. Notice that Maturidi begins by stating he has explained the wisdom in creating diverse substances. Then he clarifies a key point about God's act not being described by good or evil.
Pay attention to the phrase 'لا يوصف بذلك'.
2
Identify the definition of wisdom
Find the phrase 'هو معنى الحكمة ووضع كل شيء موضعه'. This is the core definition: wisdom is placing everything in its place.
This refutes the idea that wisdom means only creating good things.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider how this definition avoids attributing moral categories to God's actions. Why is this important for Islamic theology?
This connects to the broader theme of divine transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد بينا وجه الحكمة في خلق الجواهر المختلفة، وأن فعل الله لا يوصف بذلك وإن أنشأها على ما عليه من قبح القبيح وحسن الحسن، هو معنى الحكمة ووضع كل شيء موضعه، وأن الله تعالى إذ لم يخلق لحاجات نفسه وإنما خلق بذاته، إنه خالق ليكون الخلق الذي ركب فيهم العقول وجعلهم أهل المعرفة، بالنعم و البلايا يمتحنون، بوضع كل شيء موضعه والقيام بالشكر لما أنعم عليهم بأن جعل لهم جميع الخلائق على اختلاف جواهرهم أدله وعبرا ومحنة وابتلاء بمعاداة جواهر وموالاة أخرى، وليغرفوا كيفية الاتقاء ووجه الجذر وما فيه الرُّعْبُ ووجوه المبادرة في ذلك للعواقب المحمودة في العقول وإبقاء المكروهة فيها بما عاينوا من مختلف الجواهر والأحوال في حق الترغيب والترحيب ليكون الوعد والوعيد مقدرا عن الحسن والعيان؛ إذ ذلك طريق المعارف و به يوصل إلى درك النهايات، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And we have explained the aspect of wisdom in creating the different substances, and that the act of God is not described by that, and that He originated them upon what they are of evil evil and good good—that is the meaning of wisdom: and placing everything in its place. And that God, exalted, since He did not create for His own needs but only created by His essence, He is a Creator so that the creation—in whom He composed intellects and made them people of knowledge—by blessings and trials they are tested, by placing everything in its place and undertaking gratitude for what He bestowed upon them, by making for them all creatures, despite the difference of their substances, as proofs and signs and trial and test by enmity of some substances and friendship of others. And that they may recognize the manner of piety and the aspect of wariness and what is in it of fear and the aspects of hastening in that for praiseworthy consequences in intellects and preserving what is disliked in them, by what they witness of different substances and states in the matter of encouragement and welcome (or intimidation?), so that promise and threat may be appreciated about the beautiful and the evident; for that is the path of knowledges and by it one reaches the perception of ends. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 773

Commentary
This passage explains the divine wisdom (hikma) in creating different substances (jawāhir mukhtalifa). Maturidi states that God's act is not subject to description of good or evil in the same way; rather, creating things with their inherent qualities of evil or good is the meaning of wisdom: placing everything in its proper place. Since God created not for His own needs but by His essence, He created to test rational beings (those with intellects and knowledge) through blessings and trials. By placing everything in its place and requiring gratitude, He made all creatures, despite their different substances, as proofs (adilla), signs (ʿibar), trials (miḥan) and tests (ibtilāʾ) by having enmity towards some substances and friendship for others. Through this, creatures learn piety (itqāʾ), wariness (ḥadhar), fear (ruʿb), and how to hasten toward praiseworthy outcomes and avoid disliked ones, based on what they witness of different substances and states. This makes the divine promise and threat (al-waʿd wa al-waʿīd) appreciated as beautiful and evident. This is the path to knowledge and ultimate understanding.

Key Terms
الحكمة
قبح القبيح وحسن الحسن
وضع كل شيء موضعه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God creates evil substances, then His act is itself evil or lacking in wisdom.
Correction: Maturidi clarifies that God's act is not subject to human moral judgment; wisdom is about appropriate placement, not moral labeling.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the meaning of divine wisdom?
A) Creating only good things
B) Placing everything in its proper place
C) Avoiding the creation of evil
D) Subjecting God's actions to human moral judgment

Key Takeaway
Divine wisdom is not about God's actions being good or evil by human standards, but about each thing being placed in its proper context.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a situation you consider unjust or harmful, do you silently accuse God of failing in wisdom? How does Maturidi's definition of wisdom as 'placing everything in its place' challenge that reaction? What would it look like for you to trust that this too has a proper context, even if hidden? Will you actively remind yourself of this the next time you are tempted to judge God's placement?
?
Think of a specific event in your past that you still resent as 'bad' for you. How might it be that God placed that event exactly where it needed to be in your life’s journey? Are you willing to let go of your judgment and see it as part of a wise placement? What would it cost you to do so?
?
The passage says God's act is not described by the terms 'good' or 'evil' as humans use them. Examine your own speech: do you ever label God's acts as 'unfair' or 'cruel'? How does this passage demand a change in how you speak about God? What specific phrase from the source can you memorize to correct yourself when such thoughts arise?

The Purpose of Creation: Testing and the Path to Knowledge
Maturidi explains that God created the world as a test for rational beings to learn and appreciate divine promise and threat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's explanation of why God created the world: to test rational beings through blessings and trials, leading them to knowledge and appreciation of divine promise and threat.

Core Idea
God created different substances as tests and signs, enabling humans to learn piety and discern consequences.

Building on the concept of wisdom, Maturidi now explains the purpose behind creation. He argues that God, who is self-sufficient, created not for His own needs but to put rational beings to the test. Through the diversity of substances—some friendly, some hostile—humans learn to navigate life, recognize divine signs, and appreciate the reality of promise and threat.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the reason for creation
Notice the phrase 'إذ لم يخلق لحاجات نفسه وإنما خلق بذاته'. This tells us God created for His essence, not out of need.
2
Understand the role of diverse substances
Look for how different substances serve as proofs, signs, trials, and tests. See the contrast between enmity and friendship.
This shows the purpose of diversity.
3
Connect to learning outcomes
Maturidi mentions that through this, humans learn piety, wariness, fear, and appreciation of promise and threat. Reflect on how this leads to knowledge.
This is the ultimate goal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد بينا وجه الحكمة في خلق الجواهر المختلفة، وأن فعل الله لا يوصف بذلك وإن أنشأها على ما عليه من قبح القبيح وحسن الحسن، هو معنى الحكمة ووضع كل شيء موضعه، وأن الله تعالى إذ لم يخلق لحاجات نفسه وإنما خلق بذاته، إنه خالق ليكون الخلق الذي ركب فيهم العقول وجعلهم أهل المعرفة، بالنعم و البلايا يمتحنون، بوضع كل شيء موضعه والقيام بالشكر لما أنعم عليهم بأن جعل لهم جميع الخلائق على اختلاف جواهرهم أدله وعبرا ومحنة وابتلاء بمعاداة جواهر وموالاة أخرى، وليغرفوا كيفية الاتقاء ووجه الجذر وما فيه الرُّعْبُ ووجوه المبادرة في ذلك للعواقب المحمودة في العقول وإبقاء المكروهة فيها بما عاينوا من مختلف الجواهر والأحوال في حق الترغيب والترحيب ليكون الوعد والوعيد مقدرا عن الحسن والعيان؛ إذ ذلك طريق المعارف و به يوصل إلى درك النهايات، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And we have explained the aspect of wisdom in creating the different substances, and that the act of God is not described by that, and that He originated them upon what they are of evil evil and good good—that is the meaning of wisdom: and placing everything in its place. And that God, exalted, since He did not create for His own needs but only created by His essence, He is a Creator so that the creation—in whom He composed intellects and made them people of knowledge—by blessings and trials they are tested, by placing everything in its place and undertaking gratitude for what He bestowed upon them, by making for them all creatures, despite the difference of their substances, as proofs and signs and trial and test by enmity of some substances and friendship of others. And that they may recognize the manner of piety and the aspect of wariness and what is in it of fear and the aspects of hastening in that for praiseworthy consequences in intellects and preserving what is disliked in them, by what they witness of different substances and states in the matter of encouragement and welcome (or intimidation?), so that promise and threat may be appreciated about the beautiful and the evident; for that is the path of knowledges and by it one reaches the perception of ends. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 773

Commentary
This passage explains the divine wisdom (hikma) in creating different substances (jawāhir mukhtalifa). Maturidi states that God's act is not subject to description of good or evil in the same way; rather, creating things with their inherent qualities of evil or good is the meaning of wisdom: placing everything in its proper place. Since God created not for His own needs but by His essence, He created to test rational beings (those with intellects and knowledge) through blessings and trials. By placing everything in its place and requiring gratitude, He made all creatures, despite their different substances, as proofs (adilla), signs (ʿibar), trials (miḥan) and tests (ibtilāʾ) by having enmity towards some substances and friendship for others. Through this, creatures learn piety (itqāʾ), wariness (ḥadhar), fear (ruʿb), and how to hasten toward praiseworthy outcomes and avoid disliked ones, based on what they witness of different substances and states. This makes the divine promise and threat (al-waʿd wa al-waʿīd) appreciated as beautiful and evident. This is the path to knowledge and ultimate understanding.

Key Terms

الشكر
الوعد والوعيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception: Some think God created the world for His own benefit or out of need.
Correction: Maturidi clarifies that God is self-sufficient and created by His essence, not for any need.

Key Takeaway
The diversity in creation is not arbitrary; it is a carefully designed test to teach humans wisdom and lead them to recognize the reality of God's promise and threat.

Denying Divine Commands Negates Wisdom
Maturidi argues that denying divine commands contradicts the wisdom of the Creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that denying God's commands and prohibitions undermines the very wisdom His creation demonstrates.

Core Idea
Without divine commands, creation and annihilation become purposeless, contradicting divine wisdom.

Maturidi presents a concise theological argument linking divine commands to the wisdom of creation. He warns that rejecting God's moral guidance leads to a view where creation and destruction have no purpose, which cannot be attributed to a wise Creator. Let's examine his reasoning closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to absorb its rhythm, then read the English translation. Notice how Maturidi moves from denial to consequences.
The passage is a single continuous argument.
2
Identify the core claim
Find the statement about what happens when someone denies command, prohibition, promise, and threat. Identify the consequence Maturidi draws.
3
Trace the logical chain
Follow the argument: denial → no wisdom from creation → creation and annihilation → such action is not wise → but the world's proofs show the Maker is wise.
This chain connects denial directly to contradiction of divine wisdom.
4
Reflect on the implication
Ask yourself: Why must a wise Creator have commands and prohibitions? How does this passage defend the necessity of revelation?
The passage grounds prophethood in divine wisdom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم من أنكر الأمر والنهي والوعد والوعيد لم يحصل لإنشاء حكمة حصل منه على الإنشاء ثم الإفناء ثم معلوم أن كل من ذلك عاقبة فعله ليس بحكيم فدلت حكمة صانع العالم بما جعل فيه من الأدلة على وجدانيته على أنه حكيم والله الموفق
Then whoever denies the command and prohibition and promise and threat does not achieve wisdom from creation: he produces creation then annihilation. Then it is known that one whose action's consequence is that is not wise. Thus the wisdom of the Maker of the world—through what He placed in it of proofs of His existence—indicates that He is Wise. And God is the Giver of success.
Source pages p. 776

Commentary
This passage presents an argument from divine wisdom: whoever denies that God issues commands, prohibitions, promises, and threats cannot attribute wisdom to God's act of creation. The reasoning is that if God creates beings only to annihilate them without any purpose or moral framework, such action would not be wise. But we know from the proofs of God's existence in the world that He is indeed Wise. Therefore, denying that God gives commands and prohibitions contradicts the very wisdom that His creation demonstrates.

Key Terms

النهي
الحكمة
الإفناء
الوعد والوعيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's wisdom does not require Him to issue commands or prohibitions.
Correction: The passage argues that without commands, creation and annihilation would be purposeless, which contradicts divine wisdom.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consequence of denying divine commands and prohibitions?
A) It leads to disbelief in God.
B) It makes creation and annihilation meaningless, contradicting wisdom.
C) It is a minor sin that can be forgiven.
D) It means God is not powerful.

Key Takeaway
Divine commands and prohibitions are necessary for creation to be an act of wisdom; denying them undermines the very evidence of God's wisdom in the world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Objection and Answer on Divine Commands
Maturidi presents an objection against commands and answers it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi defends the necessity of divine commands despite God's self-sufficiency.

Core Idea
God's self-sufficiency does not negate commands; they benefit us, not Him.

This passage tackles a common objection: if God is completely self-sufficient and knows all, why would He issue commands and prohibitions? The objector argues that such actions in human context serve needs or benefits. Maturidi presents the objection fairly, then provides a decisive answer that upholds the wisdom of divine commands.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Identify the objector's reasoning: commands in the witnessed world are for revealing hidden matters or for the benefit/repelling harm of the commander. Apply this to God.
Notice the objector uses analogy from human experience.
2
Read the answer from the faqih
The answer begins with 'نقول وبالله التوفيق'. It points out that the objection assumes God acts like needy beings. But God created the world not for need.
The key shift: from 'why would God command?' to 'commands are for human welfare'.
3
Understand the decisive distinction
Needy beings act to gain benefit or avoid harm. God, being Wise and Self-Sufficient, does not act for such reasons. Thus commands remain valid as a means of guidance and test for humans.
The answer preserves both divine self-sufficiency and the purpose of commands.
4
Reflect on the misconception
Many think self-sufficiency implies no need to command. This passage shows commands are for the commanded, not the Commander.
Connect to the lesson's learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن أنكر الأمر والنهي والمحنة ذهب إلى معنى المحنة في الشاهد إنما هو لظهور ما خفي وتجلى ما استتر والأمر والنهي لمنفعة ينالها الآمر والناهي أو مكروه يدفعه فإذا كان الله غنيا بذاته عليما بالسرائر والخفيات ذهب معنى المحنة والأمر والنهي قال الفقيه رحمه الله نقول وبالله التوفيق إن كان أمره ونهيه ومحبته على ما يذكر فإن فعله لذلك يكون لمكروه يدفع أو محبوب يجلب أو عيب عنه يتخلى والله سبحانه أنشأ العالم لا للذي يذكر فمثله الأمر والنهي والمحنة ما كان ذلك التقدير إنما هو فعل المحتاجين مما يعلو درجاتهم وتجل أقدارهم ولو فعلوا غير ذلك كان عليهم في فعل ذلك ضرر عاجل وشر آجل فأما من هو حكيم بذاته غنى فهو لا يفعل النفع ولا لدفع الضرر فمثله الأمر والنهي
And whoever denies the command, prohibition, and trial goes to the meaning of trial in the witnessed world: it is only for the manifestation of what is hidden and the disclosure of what is concealed. And command and prohibition are for a benefit that the commander and prohibitor attain, or a disliked thing they repel. Since God is Self-Sufficient by His essence, Knowing of secrets and hidden things, the meaning of trial and command and prohibition disappears. The faqih (may God have mercy on him) said: We say, and with God is success: If His command, prohibition, and love are as mentioned, then His doing that would be for a disliked thing repelled, a beloved thing attracted, or a defect removed. God Almighty created the world not for what is mentioned. So the likes of command, prohibition, and trial—that estimation is only the action of the needy, by which their ranks rise and their standings become exalted. If they did otherwise, they would incur immediate harm and future evil. As for One who is Wise by His essence, Self-Sufficient, He does not act for benefit or to repel harm. So the likes of command and prohibition [are still valid].
Source pages p. 776

Commentary
This passage contains an objection and its answer. First, the objector argues: In the witnessed world, trials (mihna) are meant to reveal what is hidden, and commands and prohibitions are for the benefit of the commander or to repel harm. Since God is Self-Sufficient and knows all secrets, these purposes are irrelevant to Him, so commands and prohibitions would be meaningless. The faqih answers: This reasoning is flawed because it assumes that God's commands are like those of needy beings. In reality, God created the world not for any need, but for wisdom. The commands and prohibitions are for the benefit of human beings, not for God. Needy beings act for benefit or to avoid harm, but God is above that. Therefore, the objection from divine self-sufficiency does not negate the necessity of commands; rather, it affirms that they are for human welfare.

Key Terms
الأمر
النهي
المحنة
الغنى
الحكيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Because God is self-sufficient and knows everything, He has no need to issue commands or prohibitions, so they are unnecessary.
Correction: Commands are not for God's benefit but for the guidance and welfare of human beings. God's self-sufficiency does not preclude wisdom-based commands that benefit creation.

Checkpoint
According to the answer in this passage, why does God issue commands despite being self-sufficient?
A) To gain benefit for Himself
B) To reveal what is hidden from Him
C) To benefit human beings, not Himself
D) To avoid harm to Himself

Key Takeaway
God's self-sufficiency does not negate the need for commands; they exist for human benefit and guidance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a difficult command from God, do you internally resent it, thinking it is a burden He imposes? How does knowing that God has no need of your obedience, but commands for your own benefit, change your heart?
?
Is your obedience motivated by fear of punishment or by understanding that God's commands are designed for your welfare? What would it take for you to truly internalize that God's commands are for your good?
?
Reflect on a specific command you struggle with. Can you see how it is for your benefit? If not, what assumption about God's motives might you be holding that contradicts this lesson?

8 min
The Necessity of Divine Commands and Answering Objections
Maturidi refutes the denial of divine commands and answers the objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that divine commands are necessary to prevent chaos and that the objection of pointlessness is answered by noting God's self-sufficiency and human benefit.

Core Idea
Divine commands are for human benefit, not to inform the All-Knowing.

Maturidi addresses those who deny the need for divine commands by showing the chaos that would ensue without them, and then counters the objection that testing is pointless because God already knows all. He demonstrates that commands serve human welfare, not divine knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
This passage is a cohesive argument with two parts: a positive case for commands and a refutation of an objection.
2
Identify the two main parts
The first part argues that denying commands leads to chaos and negates wisdom. The second part presents and answers the objection that testing is pointless since God already knows.
Notice how the objection is introduced with 'And whoever denies...'
3
Understand the necessity argument
Maturidi says without commands, people would selfishly pursue survival, leading to conflict. Commands establish order so each knows their rights.
He uses the example of nourishment and desire for life.
4
Analyze the objection and answer
The objector says: human testing reveals hidden knowledge, but God already knows, so commands are useless. Maturidi answers: God's commands are not for His own benefit but for human betterment, just as He created the world not for His own benefit.
The answer emphasizes God's self-sufficiency (ghina).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما ثم من أنكر الأمر والنهي والوعد والوعيد لم يحصل لإنشاء حكمة ، حصل منه على الإنشاء ثم الإفناء ، ثم معلوم أن كل من ذلك عاقبة فعله ليس بحكيم ، فدلت حكمة صانع العالم – بما جعل فيه من الأدلة على وجدانيته على أنه حكيم، والله الموفق وعظيم سلطانه مع ما كان الله سبحانه إذ هو غنى بذاته حكيم في فعله خلق الخلق للبقاء إلى قدرة جعلها لهم ، ثم لم يجعل البقاء إلا بالأغذية ، وقد حبب إليهم البقاء ودوام الحياة ، فلو لم يجعل عليهم الأمر والنهي لبادر كل إلى ما يطمع فيه [من] البقاء ودوام الحياة ، مع ما له فيه من اللذة والشهوة ، ثم يفعل أقرانه بذلك الشيء نجو فعله فيحدث بينهم التنازع والتجاذب ، ويحملهم ذلك على التدافع وفي ذلك خوف الفناء بما به جعل البقاء ، فلزم جعل الحرمات والحل والأمر والنهي بما فيه من الوعد والوعيد ؛ ليعلم كل ما له مما ليس له ؛ فيسلم [من] كل عداوة وتبقى روحه . ومن أنكر الأمر والنهى والمحنة ذهب إلى معنى المحنة في الشاهد ، إنما هو لظهور ما خفى وتجلى ما استتر ، والأمر والنهى لمنفعة ينالها الأمر والناهي أو مكروه يدفعه ، فإذا كان الله غنيا بذاته عليها بالسرائر والخفيات ذهب معنى المحنة والأمر والنهي . قال الفقيه رحمه الله : نقول ، وبالله التوفيق ، إن كان أمره ونهيه ومحبته على له مع ما يذكر فإن فعله لذلك يكون لمكروه يدفع أو محبوب يجلب أو عيب عنه يتخلى، والله سبحانه أنشأ العالم لا للذى يذكر ، فمثله الأمر والنهى والمحنة ما كان ذلك التقدير إنما هو فعل المحتاجين مما يعلو درجاتهم وتجل أقدارهم ، ولو فعلوا غير ذلك كان عليهم في فعل ذلك ضرر عاجل وشر آجل ، فأما من هو حكيم بذاته ، غنى ، فهو لا يفعل النفع ولا لدفع الضرر ، فمثله الأمر والنهي .
Then, whoever denies commands and prohibitions and promises and warnings does not achieve the establishment of wisdom; he achieves from it establishment and then destruction. It is known that each of these, the consequence of his action, is not wise. So the wisdom of the Maker of the world – by what He placed in it of proofs of His existence – indicates that He is wise, and God is the giver of success. And His great sovereignty, while God – exalted is He – since He is independent by His essence, wise in His action, created creation for permanence by a power He gave them, then He did not make permanence except through nourishment, and He made them love permanence and continuity of life. So if He had not imposed upon them commands and prohibitions, each would hasten to what he desires [for] permanence and continuity of life, along with the pleasure and desire he has in it, then his peers would do the same thing, then conflict and contention would arise among them, and that would lead them to repulsion, and in that is fear of annihilation by that which He made permanence. So it was necessary to establish the sacred and the permitted, and commands and prohibitions including promises and warnings, so that each knows what is his and what is not his, so he is safe from all enmity and his spirit remains. And whoever denies commands and prohibitions and trial goes to the meaning of trial in the witnessed world: it is only for the manifestation of what was hidden and the revelation of what was concealed. And commands and prohibitions are for a benefit that the commander or prohibiter receives or a disliked thing he repels. So if God is independent by His essence, knowing the innermost secrets and hidden things, the meaning of trial and commands and prohibitions disappears. The jurist (may God have mercy on him) said: We say, and with God is success, if His command and prohibition and love are [such] that His doing that would be to repel a disliked thing or to attract a beloved thing or to divest Himself of a defect, and God – exalted is He – originated the world not for that which is mentioned, so similar to that are commands and prohibitions and trial. That estimation is only the action of those in need, raising their ranks and glorifying their statuses, and if they did otherwise, there would be immediate harm and future evil in that action. As for He who is wise by His essence, independent, He does not act for benefit nor to repel harm, so similar to that are commands and prohibitions.
Source pages p. 776

Commentary
This passage is an argument and refutation. Maturidi first argues that to deny divine commands and prohibitions, along with promises and warnings, would negate the establishment of wisdom. He points out that a person who does such a thing, ending in destruction, cannot be called wise. Therefore, the wisdom of the Creator, evident from the proofs of His existence in the world, shows that He is wise. Maturidi then elaborates: God, being self-sufficient and wise, created humans with a desire for life and provided them with sustenance. Had He not given commands and prohibitions, people would selfishly pursue what ensures their survival, leading to conflict and mutual harm. Hence, it is necessary to have rules (sacred and permissible) to avoid chaos. Next, Maturidi presents an objection from those who deny commands: they compare divine trial to human trial, where testing reveals hidden knowledge. Since God already knows all hidden things, trial seems pointless. Maturidi answers this by stating that God's commands are not for His own benefit or to repel harm, as He is self-sufficient. Rather, the purpose is for the benefit of humans, who need such guidance to elevate their ranks and avoid harm. The point is that just as God created the world not for His own benefit, so too are His commands for the benefit of creation.

Key Terms
أمر
نهي
وعد
وعيد
حكمة
محنة
غنى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Divine commands are unnecessary because God already knows everything people will do.
Correction: Maturidi explains that commands are for human benefit—to establish order and elevate human ranks—not to inform God of hidden matters.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi argue that divine commands and prohibitions are necessary?
A) Because God needs humans to obey Him
B) To prevent conflict and ensure survival through orderly rules
C) Because humans are inherently evil
D) To test God's own knowledge

Key Takeaway
Divine commands are essential for social harmony and are a mercy from God, not a reflection of any need on His part.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you break a divine command, do you recognize that you are acting against your own well-being and that of your community? What specific steps can you take today to repent and restore that balance?
?
The passage teaches that God gave commands to prevent conflict and preserve life. Is there a relationship in your life that suffers because you neglect the boundaries God set? What would it cost you to realign with His command?
