Why Creation's Diversity Demands Divine Commands
Maturidi argues that the diversity of creation (benefit/harm) necessitates commands and prohibitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's rational argument that the coexistence of benefit and harm in creation, along with human susceptibility to pain and pleasure, necessarily implies that God issues commands and prohibitions for human guidance.

Core Idea
Since God made creation with both benefit and harm, He must also provide commands to guide us.

Maturidi continues his rational exploration of God's attributes by considering the very structure of creation. He observes that everything is mixed with both benefit and harm, and every being is susceptible to pain and pleasure. This observation, he argues, leads to the conclusion that God must have a purpose in such a creation—namely, to warn and encourage humans through promises and threats, which in turn necessitates divine commands and prohibitions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage has two main parts: the first argument from creation diversity, and a second point about God's self-sufficiency.
2
Identify the key observation
Find where Maturidi states that God made creation into two divisions: harmful and beneficial, and made each being susceptible to pain and pleasure.
Look for the terms ضار and نافع, and ألم and لذة.
3
Understand the inference
Why does this observation lead to the conclusion that there must be outcomes? Maturidi says it is not possible that He made them so except for outcomes (عواقب).
The outcomes are warnings (وعيد) and promises (وعد).
4
Connect to commands
These outcomes require commands and prohibitions to guide humans toward benefit and away from harm. Maturidi then adds that even though God is self-sufficient, He commands for our benefit.
This shows that commands are for creatures, not for God.
5
Reflect on the theological point
Consider how this argument refutes the idea that God's self-sufficiency makes commands unnecessary. Maturidi shows that commands are a natural consequence of the way creation is structured.
This is a key point in Islamic theology about divine wisdom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبينا من اختلاف الممتحنين في الغنا والحكمة لم يجز تقدير أحدهما بالآخر ، ولا يحتمل حكيم [يفعل الشر الحكمة الربوبية ، فتكلفه الذي ذكر خطأ وبعد ، فإنه إذ جعل الخلق قسمين : ضارا ونافعا ، وجعل كل [نجدهر] محتملا للألم واللذة ، لم يحتمل أن يجعلهم كذلك إلا لعواقب . يحذرهم بها ويرغبهم فيها من الوعيد بالشدائد والوعد بالملاذ ، وبذلك تتم الرغبة والرهبة ، والله الموفق . وبعد ، فإذ خلق الخلق ، وجعل البعض منافعا لبعض وإن لم يكن له في ذلك نفع لغناه . وكذلك المضار ، فمثله يأمر وينهى بمنافع بعض ببعض واتقاء المضار ، مع ما يأمر بما ينفعهم . كما خلقهم وجعل لهم عن ذلك ، وينهى يضرهم ،
And we have shown from the difference of the tested ones in wealth and wisdom that it is not permissible to measure one by the other, nor does a wise one who does evil [in?] the wisdom of lordship be possible. So his assumption that he mentioned is error and far-off. For He, when He made creation two divisions: harmful and beneficial, and made everything [؟] susceptible to pain and pleasure, it is not possible that He made them so except for outcomes. He warns them thereby and makes them desire therein from threatening with hardships and promising with delights, and thereby desire and fear are completed, and God is the giver of success. And after that, when He created creation and made some benefits for others, even though He has no benefit in that due to His self-sufficiency. And likewise the harms, so similarly He commands and forbids for the benefits of some by others and avoidance of harms, along with commanding what benefits them. Just as He created them and made for them from that, and forbids what harms them.
Source pages p. 777

Commentary
This passage presents a further proof for the necessity of divine commands. Maturidi states that it has been shown that happiness and wisdom cannot be equated. He then argues that since God created two categories of things (harmful and beneficial) and made each being susceptible to pain and pleasure, it is impossible that He did this without a purpose. That purpose must be to warn and encourage humans through promises of delights and threats of hardships, thereby completing the dynamics of desire and fear. Maturidi then adds that even though God is self-sufficient, He created some things as benefits for others. Similarly, He issues commands and prohibitions to ensure that people benefit each other and avoid harm. God commands what benefits and forbids what harms, just as He created them to need such guidance.

Correction: Maturidi shows that commands are for the sake of creatures, not for God. The very structure of creation (benefit and harm, pain and pleasure) rationally requires commands to guide humans toward benefit and away from harm.

The Necessity of Gratitude and Knowledge of God
Maturidi argues that excellence of creation and blessings necessitate knowledge of God and commands.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the excellence of creation and divine blessings to establish the rational necessity of knowing God and obeying His commands.

Core Idea
Great blessings demand recognition; otherwise they are wasted.

Maturidi presents a profound argument rooted in wisdom itself. He points to the perfection of human creation and the abundance of blessings bestowed without prior obligation. Intellectually, it would be unjust to grant such favors without the recipient acknowledging the Giver. This leads to the necessity of knowing God, which is fulfilled through divine commands, trials, promises, and warnings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the flow of Maturidi's argument.
Notice the key terms: حكمة, أمر, نهى, نعمة, شكر, محبة, محنة.
2
Identify the rational principle
Maturidi states that it is not permissible in the intellect to bestow great favors upon one who does not know them. Why? Because it would be wasteful and unjust. Identify this principle and understand its implications.
3
Trace the conclusion
From the rational principle, Maturidi concludes that knowledge of the Benefactor is incumbent. This leads to trial (commands/prohibitions) and is supported by promises and warnings. See how the argument unfolds.
The conclusion has three parts: knowledge, trial, and promises/warnings.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself: Why does Maturidi emphasize that blessings come without prior recompense? How does this strengthen the argument for divine guidance?
This highlights God's generosity and humanity's inherent indebtedness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا إن في الحكمة الأمر والنهى : إن الله خلق البشر في أحسن تقويم ، والله الموفق وسخر كم جميع جميع ما على وجه الأرض وبركاتها وبركات السماء ذلك مخرج من غير أن سبق منهم المكافأة أو مخرج حق قضاه ، فلا يجوز في العقل إسداء مثل هذه النعم إلى ما لا يعرفها لما فيه تضييع وظلم النعم ، فلزمهم به معرفة المنعم ليعلموا من يستحق المحبة ويستوجب الشكر ، وفى ذلك لزوم المحنة ، ووصل بذلك الوعد والوعيد ليتم الرغبة والرهبة ، وبالله التوفيق .
And also, in wisdom there are commands and prohibitions: Indeed God created humans in the best stature, and God is the giver of success, and He subjected all that is on the face of the earth and its blessings and the blessings of the sky. That is brought forth without any prior recompense from them or a due He had decreed. So it is not permissible in the intellect to bestow such favors upon one who does not know them, because that involves wasting and injustice to the favors. So the knowledge of the Benefactor is incumbent upon them, so that they know who deserves love and merits gratitude. And in that is the necessity of trial, and He connected to that promises and warnings to complete desire and fear. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 777

Commentary
This passage presents a third argument. Maturidi states that wisdom itself requires commands and prohibitions. He points out that God created humans in the best form and subjected to them all earthly blessings and heavenly blessings. These blessings are given without any prior deserving or obligation on man's part. Intellectually, it is not fitting to grant such great favors to someone who does not recognize them, as that would be wasteful and unjust to the favors. Therefore, it becomes obligatory for humans to know the Benefactor, so that they may love Him and give thanks. This entails a trial (test) through divine commands, and God attaches promises and warnings to complete the motivations of desire and fear.

Correction: Maturidi clarifies that blessings demand recognition and gratitude; to bestow them without such would be wasteful and unjust.

Refuting Jesus's Divinity Through Human Attributes
Maturidi refutes the claim that Jesus is divine by listing his human attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi refutes the claim that Jesus is divine by showing that all of Jesus's human characteristics and actions are incompatible with divinity.

Core Idea
Jesus's human needs and worship prove he is a servant, not a god.

Imam Maturidi addresses a central Christian claim with a simple but powerful argument. He points to the undeniable human aspects of Jesus's life and actions as recorded in the Gospels themselves. This lesson will examine how Maturidi uses Jesus's own behavior to reject his divinity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation to grasp the flow of Maturidi's argument.
Notice the structure: the disagreement is divided into two aspects, but only the first (divinity) is addressed here.
2
Identify the human attributes listed
Maturidi lists several attributes of Jesus that show his humanity. List each one and consider how each contradicts divinity.
Examples: eating, drinking, needing to relieve himself, physical growth, worship, humility.
3
Understand the conclusion
Reflect on Maturidi's conclusion: if such a claim could be made for Jesus, it could be made for any human. Why does this strengthen the refutation?
This is an argument from reductio ad absurdum.
4
Connect to Islamic theology
Consider how this argument fits within the broader Islamic insistence on Tawhid and the absolute distinction between Creator and creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأصل في هذا عندنا أن الاختلاف رجع إلى وجهين: أحدهما الربوبية، والله تعالى جل ثناؤه قد بين إحالة ذلك بأكله وشربه، ودفع الحاجات إلى مكان، ووصفه بالصغر والكهولة، وعبادته لله تعالى وتضرعه له وخضوعه، ودعائه الخلق إلى عبادة الله وتوحيده، وبشارته بمحمد صلى الله عليه وسلم وإيمانه بالرسل، ثم جعل جل ثناؤه عليه جميع آيات الحدث وإمارات العبودة لنفسه ما جعل في جميع العالم، وكذلك هو صلى الله عليه وسلم لم يدع العبودة والرسالة. فالقول له بالإلهية قول لا معنى له مع ما لو جاز ذلك لجاز لكل من البشر.
And the principle in this, according to us, is that the disagreement returns to two aspects: one of them is divinity (al-rububiyya), and Allah, exalted be His praise, has shown the impossibility of that by his eating and drinking, and relieving needs in a place, and his description with smallness and old age, and his worship of Allah, his supplication and humility to Him, and his calling of creation to worship Allah and His oneness, and his giving glad tidings of Muhammad (peace be upon him) and his belief in the messengers. Then He, exalted be His praise, placed upon him all the signs of origination and the marks of servitude for Himself that He placed upon all the world. Likewise, he (peace be upon him) did not claim servitude and messengership [only] but rather [accepted it]. So the statement of divinity for him is a statement without meaning, especially since if that were permissible, it would be permissible for every human being.
Source pages p. 812

Commentary
This passage is a concise refutation of the Christian claim that Jesus is divine. Maturidi sets up a two-part classification: the Christian error lies in either attributing divinity (rububiyya) or sonship (bunuwwa) to Jesus. He then addresses the first aspect, divinity, by listing concrete human characteristics of Jesus: he ate, drank, relieved himself, was described as a child and then an adult, worshipped God, prayed, humbled himself, called people to worship God alone, gave news of Muhammad, and believed in the prophets. All these are clear marks of being a created servant ('abd) and messenger (rasul). Moreover, God placed upon Jesus all the signs of contingency (ayat al-hadath) and servitude that appear in all creatures. Jesus himself never claimed divinity but rather affirmed his servitude and mission. Thus, claiming divinity for him is meaningless, and if such a claim could be made for Jesus, it could be made for any human.

Key Terms

العبودة
الرسالة
آيات الحدث
إمارات العبودة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that because Jesus performed miracles and had a special birth, he must be divine.
Correction: Maturidi argues that miracles do not negate servitude; Jesus's human needs and acts of worship clearly show he is a created being and a messenger, not God.

Checkpoint

A) Jesus's miracles.
B) Jesus's human needs and actions.
C) Jesus's claim to be God.
D) The consensus of the prophets.

Key Takeaway
Jesus's human attributes, worship, and acceptance of messengership clearly show he is a servant of God, not divine.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Will I consciously use that moment to say 'Alhamdulillah' and feel my need for Him?
?

Refutation of Physical Generation (Wilad) for God's Son
Maturidi refutes physical generation as a meaning of sonship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that physical generation is an impossible concept for God.

Core Idea
God is free from the needs and desires that drive physical generation.

Maturidi begins his refutation by examining the claim of sonship through physical generation. He identifies the causes that lead creatures to seek offspring and shows they cannot apply to God. This lesson unpacks his logical argument against wilad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
The claim is that Jesus is God's son. Maturidi examines one meaning: physical generation.
2
List the causes of generation
Maturidi lists need (haja), lust (shahwa), and loneliness (wahsha) as reasons for seeking children. Notice each is impossible for God.
OCR may distort some words.
3
Understand the impossibility
God is free from need, cannot be overcome by lust, and is not subject to loneliness. Therefore, physical generation is impossible.
4
Note additional arguments
Maturidi adds that generation requires a substance from the father, and God is unlike creation. Also, if God wanted a diversion, He would not take from our realm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثانى أن يكون ابنه، وذلك يخرج على وجوه: أحدها الولاد، وذلك محال فاسد لغنى الرب عن أن تمسه الحاجة أو تغلبه الشهوة أو تعتريه الوحشة، وهن أسباب طلب الولاد، على إحالة كون الولاد من غير جوهر الوالد، والله تعالى بذاته خارج عن شبه الخلق، أو عن المعنى الذى يحتمل ذلك الوجه، وعلى ما بين الله أنه لو اتخذ لهوا لما احتمل أن يتخذ مما عندنا. رب يوجب ذلك، وبعد، فإن كل ذى ولد يحتمل الشرك وزوال ملكه إليه، ومن هو بذاته ملك قادر لا يحتمل ذلك. ومن يقول لا معنى له أن يكون جزء من الشيء ولده، ويجب أن يكون غير كامل حتى يوجد، وجهة الآيات لا لأن طريق معرفة البنوة في الشاهد ليس الآيات مع ما قد شورك فيها. وبعد، هو يدعى الصدق فى الخلوص له بالعبودة، لا غير، أو من جهة الفضل ينسب إلى ذلك، والأمر المعروف في الشاهد أن ذلك ليس من أسماء التعظيم، بل تسميته المسيح والرسول أجل وأعظم في ذلك. فالآيات توجب ذلك. و بعد، فقد أعطيت لكثير من الخلق من الله تعالى كرامات خصوا بها، لم يوجب شيء منها اسم البنوة، على أن البنوة فى الكلام إنما هو من الصغار أصحاب القوة والرفعة، وهكذا شأن أثر البنين فيكون بها إكرامه. والضعاف، لا من وتعظيمه بصغره؛ إذ قد يكون ذلك من العظماء فى الصغار، ولا قوة إلا بالله.. أو أن يكون الله من حيث مفزعه وملجأه فى كل أمر ونائبة، فمن ذا الوجة
And the second [aspect] is that he is His son, and that proceeds upon aspects: one of them is physical generation (al-wilad), and that is impossible and corrupt because the Lord is free from need for need to touch Him, or lust to overcome Him, or loneliness to befall Him, and these are the causes of seeking offspring, along with the impossibility of generation from other than the substance of the father. And Allah, exalted, is in His essence outside the likeness of creation, or outside the meaning that admits that aspect. And as Allah has made clear that if He had taken a diversion, He would not take it from what is with us. A lord necessitates that. And moreover, every possessor of an offspring admits the possibility of sharing and the removal of his dominion to him, and He who is in His essence a powerful king does not admit that. And he who says, 'It is meaningless that a part of something be its offspring, and it must be imperfect until it exists,' and the aspect of the signs is not because the way of knowing sonship in the witnessed realm is not through signs when others have shared in them. And moreover, he claims truth in devotion to Him through servitude, nothing else, or from the aspect of virtue he is attributed to that, and the known matter in the witnessed realm is that that is not among the names of veneration; rather, naming him the Messiah and the Messenger is more exalted and greater in that. So the signs necessitate that. And moreover, many of creation have been given honors from Allah, with which they are distinguished; none of them necessitated the name of sonship, considering that sonship in speech is only from the small ones, the owners of strength and high rank, and thus is the affair of the effect of sons, so through it comes his honor. And the weak ones? Not from [؟] and magnifying him by his smallness; for that may be from the great ones in children, and there is no power except through Allah. Or that Allah is, from the aspect of his refuge and shelter in every matter and calamity, so from this aspect [؟].
Source pages p. 813

Commentary
This passage is a detailed refutation of the claim that Jesus is the son of God (bunuwwa). Maturidi enumerates several possible meanings of sonship and refutes each. The first meaning is physical generation (wilad), which is impossible for God because He is free from need, lust, and loneliness — the causes of seeking children. Moreover, generation requires a substance from the father, which is impossible since God is unlike creation. If God wanted a diversion, He would not take it from what we have. Second, every being that has a child is subject to possibility of sharing and loss of dominion, which cannot apply to God. Third, the argument from signs and miracles does not prove sonship because many others have performed miracles (like disciples). Fourth, Jesus himself claimed only servitude and devotion, not sonship. Fifth, the term 'son' in language denotes smallness and weakness, not honor; the titles 'Messiah' and 'Messenger' are far greater honors. Sixth, many creatures have received special honors (karamat) without being called sons of God. Finally, the possibility that 'son' means refuge is considered but left open. The argument systematically closes all justifications for the literal sonship of Jesus.

Key Terms
الولاد
الحاجة
الشهوة
الوحشة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Need
B) Lust
C) Loneliness
D) Love

Key Takeaway
Physical generation is impossible for God because He is free from the needs and desires that motivate it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel lonely or in need, do you ever imagine that God might relate to you out of similar emotions? How does Maturidi's assertion that God is free from need, lust, and loneliness challenge you to adjust your understanding of His relationship with you?
?
Maturidi argues that God's essence is unlike creation, so He cannot be subject to physical processes. In what areas of your life are you still treating God as if He operates within the limits of the physical world? What concrete change can you make today to seek Him beyond what is material?
?
The passage dismisses the idea that God would take a diversion from 'what is with us.' Do you rely on worldly distractions to fill a void that only God can fill? What would it mean for you to turn from these distractions to the One who is utterly self-sufficient?

Refutation: Sonship Implies Potential Sharing of Dominion
Maturidi argues against sonship based on impossibility of sharing dominion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that attributing a son to God would imply potential sharing of His dominion, which is impossible.

Core Idea
Any being with an offspring can potentially share dominion; God cannot.

Maturidi presents a logical argument: if God had a son, it would imply that His dominion could be shared or transferred. This is impossible for the Almighty. This lesson examines that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument
The passage states that any creature with an offspring admits the possibility of sharing and removal of dominion. God cannot have such possibility.
2
Understand the implication
Having a son implies a relationship that could lead to sharing authority. For God, this is impossible.
3
Reflect on God's essence
God is by essence a powerful king, so no such possibility exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثانى أن يكون ابنه، وذلك يخرج على وجوه: أحدها الولاد، وذلك محال فاسد لغنى الرب عن أن تمسه الحاجة أو تغلبه الشهوة أو تعتريه الوحشة، وهن أسباب طلب الولاد، على إحالة كون الولاد من غير جوهر الوالد، والله تعالى بذاته خارج عن شبه الخلق، أو عن المعنى الذى يحتمل ذلك الوجه، وعلى ما بين الله أنه لو اتخذ لهوا لما احتمل أن يتخذ مما عندنا. رب يوجب ذلك، وبعد، فإن كل ذى ولد يحتمل الشرك وزوال ملكه إليه، ومن هو بذاته ملك قادر لا يحتمل ذلك. ومن يقول لا معنى له أن يكون جزء من الشيء ولده، ويجب أن يكون غير كامل حتى يوجد، وجهة الآيات لا لأن طريق معرفة البنوة في الشاهد ليس الآيات مع ما قد شورك فيها. وبعد، هو يدعى الصدق فى الخلوص له بالعبودة، لا غير، أو من جهة الفضل ينسب إلى ذلك، والأمر المعروف في الشاهد أن ذلك ليس من أسماء التعظيم، بل تسميته المسيح والرسول أجل وأعظم في ذلك. فالآيات توجب ذلك. و بعد، فقد أعطيت لكثير من الخلق من الله تعالى كرامات خصوا بها، لم يوجب شيء منها اسم البنوة، على أن البنوة فى الكلام إنما هو من الصغار أصحاب القوة والرفعة، وهكذا شأن أثر البنين فيكون بها إكرامه. والضعاف، لا من وتعظيمه بصغره؛ إذ قد يكون ذلك من العظماء فى الصغار، ولا قوة إلا بالله.. أو أن يكون الله من حيث مفزعه وملجأه فى كل أمر ونائبة، فمن ذا الوجة
And the second [aspect] is that he is His son, and that proceeds upon aspects: one of them is physical generation (al-wilad), and that is impossible and corrupt because the Lord is free from need for need to touch Him, or lust to overcome Him, or loneliness to befall Him, and these are the causes of seeking offspring, along with the impossibility of generation from other than the substance of the father. And Allah, exalted, is in His essence outside the likeness of creation, or outside the meaning that admits that aspect. And as Allah has made clear that if He had taken a diversion, He would not take it from what is with us. A lord necessitates that. And moreover, every possessor of an offspring admits the possibility of sharing and the removal of his dominion to him, and He who is in His essence a powerful king does not admit that. And he who says, 'It is meaningless that a part of something be its offspring, and it must be imperfect until it exists,' and the aspect of the signs is not because the way of knowing sonship in the witnessed realm is not through signs when others have shared in them. And moreover, he claims truth in devotion to Him through servitude, nothing else, or from the aspect of virtue he is attributed to that, and the known matter in the witnessed realm is that that is not among the names of veneration; rather, naming him the Messiah and the Messenger is more exalted and greater in that. So the signs necessitate that. And moreover, many of creation have been given honors from Allah, with which they are distinguished; none of them necessitated the name of sonship, considering that sonship in speech is only from the small ones, the owners of strength and high rank, and thus is the affair of the effect of sons, so through it comes his honor. And the weak ones? Not from [؟] and magnifying him by his smallness; for that may be from the great ones in children, and there is no power except through Allah. Or that Allah is, from the aspect of his refuge and shelter in every matter and calamity, so from this aspect [؟].
Source pages p. 813

Commentary
This passage is a detailed refutation of the claim that Jesus is the son of God (bunuwwa). Maturidi enumerates several possible meanings of sonship and refutes each. The first meaning is physical generation (wilad), which is impossible for God because He is free from need, lust, and loneliness — the causes of seeking children. Moreover, generation requires a substance from the father, which is impossible since God is unlike creation. If God wanted a diversion, He would not take it from what we have. Second, every being that has a child is subject to possibility of sharing and loss of dominion, which cannot apply to God. Third, the argument from signs and miracles does not prove sonship because many others have performed miracles (like disciples). Fourth, Jesus himself claimed only servitude and devotion, not sonship. Fifth, the term 'son' in language denotes smallness and weakness, not honor; the titles 'Messiah' and 'Messenger' are far greater honors. Sixth, many creatures have received special honors (karamat) without being called sons of God. Finally, the possibility that 'son' means refuge is considered but left open. The argument systematically closes all justifications for the literal sonship of Jesus.

Key Terms
الشرك
زوال الملك
ملك قادر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi say about every possessor of an offspring?
A) They are necessarily weak.
B) They admit the possibility of sharing and removal of dominion.
C) They are always powerful.
D) They are mortal.

Key Takeaway
Sonship implies potential sharing of authority, which is incompatible with God's absolute sovereignty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider God's absolute kingship, are there areas of your life where you still act as if you share dominion with Him? What would it look like to fully surrender that territory to Him today?
?
The argument shows that sonship implies potential rivalry. In your heart, are there any 'partners' you elevate—like status, wealth, or relationships—that subtly share God's authority over your decisions? What will you do to dethrone them?

Refutation: Miracles Do Not Prove Sonship
Maturidi refutes the evidential value of miracles for proving sonship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that miracles (ayat) are not sufficient proof for sonship, as others have performed similar signs.

Core Idea
Miracles can be performed by others, so they don't prove divine sonship.

Some might claim that Jesus's miracles prove his sonship. Maturidi counters that many others have performed miracles (like disciples) without being called sons of God. Therefore, signs are not a valid proof for sonship.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Maturidi states that the way of knowing sonship through signs is not valid because others have shared in performing similar signs.
2
Understand the reasoning
If miracles were proof of sonship, then anyone who performs a miracle would be a son of God. But that is not the case.
3
Consider the implication
Thus, the argument from signs fails to establish sonship uniquely for Jesus.

?
Maturidi says that in the witnessed world, sonship is not known through signs. What does this teach you about how you judge your own spiritual lineage—are you basing it on external shows of power or on something deeper like submission and obedience?

Refutation: Jesus's Own Claim of Servitude and Superior Titles
Maturidi refutes sonship by citing Jesus's own claim and the greater honor of other titles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses Jesus's own claim of servitude and the superior titles 'Messiah' and 'Messenger' to refute sonship.

Core Idea
Jesus claimed only servitude, and titles like Messiah and Messenger are more honorable than 'son'.

Maturidi points out that Jesus himself claimed only devotion and servitude to God, not sonship. Furthermore, the titles 'Messiah' and 'Messenger' are greater in honor than 'son'. This lesson examines that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Maturidi says Jesus claims truth in devotion through servitude, not sonship.
2
Understand the significance
If Jesus himself only claimed servitude, then calling him son contradicts his own claims.
3
Consider the titles
Maturidi states that 'Messiah' and 'Messenger' are more exalted and greater as names of veneration.

Refutation: Other Honors Do Not Imply Sonship and Linguistic Analysis
Maturidi refutes sonship by noting other honors and linguistic implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that other creatures have received special honors without being called sons, and that the term 'son' in language denotes smallness, not honor.

Core Idea
Many have received karamat (honors) without being sons, and 'son' implies smallness, not honor.

Maturidi makes two final points: first, many of God's creation have been given special honors (karamat) without being called sons of God. Second, the word 'son' (ibn/bunuwwa) in Arabic denotes smallness and weakness, not greatness. This lesson explores these linguistic and comparative arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
The passage states that many creatures have been given honors without necessitating sonship.
2
Understand the linguistic point
Maturidi says that the term 'sonship' in speech is only from the small ones, implying smallness and dependence.
The translation is complex due to OCR issues, but the key is that 'son' denotes smallness.
3
Reflect on the refuge meaning
The passage ends with a possibility that 'son' could mean refuge, but leaves it open.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi say about the term 'sonship' (bunuwwa) in language?
A) It is a title of honor.
B) It is from the small ones, implying smallness.
C) It indicates power.
D) It is used only for prophets.

Key Takeaway
Other honors do not prove sonship, and the term 'son' linguistically implies smallness and need.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you have ever felt that God's special favors on you mean you are 'chosen' above others, how does this passage challenge that feeling? Will you now see every blessing as a sign of God's mercy, not proof of a special status?
?
The passage says sonship implies smallness and need. In your own relationship with Allah, do you ever act as if you are 'big' or independent, needing no one? What would it mean for you to truly embrace the status of a servant (abd) instead of a son?
?
When you face a calamity, do you run to Allah as a refuge? The passage suggests that if sonship means refuge, that is metaphorical. Are you truly taking Allah as your sole refuge, or do you rely on worldly shelters? What will you change today to make Allah your only refuge?

The Claim of Al-Aslah: God's Actions Must Benefit Others
Maturidi presents the claim that God's actions must benefit others.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the initial Mu'tazilite claim that God's actions must be for the benefit of others, and how this is based on an analogy to human wisdom.

Core Idea
The claimants argue that a wise agent cannot act without benefit, so God must always benefit others.

Maturidi begins by presenting the view of a group who claim to uphold tawhid but have strayed. They assert that since God is wise, His actions must have a purpose—benefit to others—because, as they argue, acting without benefit is frivolous. This sets the stage for a critical analysis of attributing human-like motives to God.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: the group's deviation, their premise, and their conclusion.
The passage starts with 'مسألة أفعال الله'.
2
Identify the two deviations
The group says most adherents of tawhid depart from it in two ways: ignorance of God's obligations or inability to refute dualists and atheists. Find these in the text.
The two ways are mentioned at the beginning.
3
Understand the core argument
The core argument: a wise agent does not act without benefit or cause. Therefore, God, being wise, cannot initiate harm and must always act for the most beneficial outcome for others.
This is the basis for al-aslah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة
أفعال الله
عن أن
زعم قوم من أهل التوحيد أن أكثر منتحليه خرج منه من وجهين: إما جهلا بواجبه، وإما عجزا عن تلخيص القول فيه من مذهب الثنوية وسائر الملحدين. فزعم قوم أنه إذ كان كل مما يعقل لغير نفع [فعله يقع] فليس بحكيم، ومن فعل فعلا لغير علة فهو عابث، فظنوا أن لا يجوز لله أن يبتدأ فعل ضرر بأحد، وأن ذلك يزيل الحكمة عنه، فألزموه في كل فعل يفعله الأصلح لغيره في الدين والأحسن لغيره في العاقبة؛ إذ هو متعال عن قول ينفعه أو يضره شيء، فلم يروا له الفعل إلا بما ينفع غيره، أو يدفع به الضرر عن غيره، فيكون ذلك أيضا علة فعله، على ما كان علة فعل كل حكيم منا، ما تأمل من نفع عاجل أو آجل أو دفع [ضرر] لزم به، فيجر بذلك حسن الثناء جزيل الثواب. وضربوا لتقدير فعله بفعل غيره مثلا بما لا يجوز أن يكون منه الكذب أو الجور، أو يكون منه الحركة [من] غير زوال، أو السكون [من] غير قرار، فثبت أن تقدير فعله على فعل الحكماء في الشاهد لازم، إلا أنهم دفعوا عنه الارتفاع بالفعل، والانحطاط بترك فعل ما، فأوجبوا بذلك أنه بفعله لا يجر إلى نفسه النفع ولا يدفع عنها الضرر، فيجب أن يكون فعله الحكمة بما ينفع غيره أو يدفع عن غيره الضرر، وجعلوا ذلك علة فعله؛ ليخرج عندهم فعله عن معنى العبث. وبهذا الوجه خالفوا الثنوية؛ إذ أبوا الفعل بغير نفع للفاعل فيه أن يكون من الحكمة، فأثبتوا الفعل بجوهر الحكمة عند المزاج، ليكون في خلاصه من جنس جوهر السفه، فيصير فعله حكمة على التقدير بالشاهد ما كون شيء لا من شيء ممتنعا في الشاهد، فأوجبوا لكلية العالم أصلا جعل وإنشاء؛ لأنه لا فصل بين خروج الفعل عن حق الوجود في الشاهد، فيلزم دفعه أن يكون ذلك من حكيم. فخالفهم أهل التوحيد في هذين، ثم ألزم فريق منهم إياه ما في العقل علة لم يكن له العقل دونها لما وجدوا فعل مثله في الشاهد عبثا، وألزموا في فعل المضار لو كان لغير نفع، يعقب سفها على ما ذكرت الثنوية في فعل لا ينتفع به الفاعل منه. ثم تفرقوا، فزعم قوم أنه لا ضرر في الحقيقة على المفعول به، وإن منه التضرع والشكوى. وزعم قوم أن عليه في الحقيقة ضررا، لكن عليه أن يعوضه عن ذلك؛ ليصير الفعل به حكمة، كالموجود في الشاهد ممن يحمل المؤن العظام وشرب الأدوية الكريهة مع القصد، وقصد الخراج لتقع العواقب، وليس له فعل الضار بغير إلا بعوض.
Issue: God's actions. Regarding that a group from among the people of tawhid claimed that most of its adherents departed from it in two ways: either ignorance of what is obligatory for Him, or inability to summarize the statement about it from the school of the dualists and the rest of the atheists. So a group claimed that if every rational being acts without benefit [his action falls] then he is not wise, and whoever does an action without a cause is frivolous. So they thought that it is not permissible for God to initiate a harmful action against anyone, and that would remove wisdom from Him. So they obligated upon Him in every action He does the most beneficial for others in religion and the best for others in the final outcome; since He is exalted above a saying that benefits Him or harms Him. So they saw no action for Him except that which benefits others, or repels harm from others. That also becomes the cause of His action, just as is the cause of every wise person among us who considers immediate or delayed benefit or repels an incurred harm, thereby earning good praise and abundant reward. And they set an example for estimating His action by the action of others, including that lying or injustice cannot come from Him, nor motion without displacement, nor stillness without stability. So it was established that estimating His action on the model of wise people in the witnessed world is necessary, except that they removed from Him exaltation by action and abasement by leaving an action. So they thereby obligated that by His action He does not draw benefit to Himself nor repel harm from Himself, so His action must be wisdom by benefiting others or repelling harm from others. They made that the cause of His action, so that in their view His action would exit from the meaning of frivolity. And in this respect they opposed the dualists, since the dualists rejected that an action without benefit to the agent could be from wisdom. So the dualists affirmed action with the substance of wisdom at the time of mixture, so that in his salvation from the species of the substance of folly, his action becomes wisdom according to the estimation of the witnessed world: that something cannot come from nothing in the witnessed world. So they obligated for the whole world an origin of creation and formation, because there is no distinction between the action exiting from the right of existence in the witnessed world, so it necessitates that it be from a wise [agent]. So the people of tawhid opposed them in these two points. Then a group among them obligated upon Him that in the intellect there is a cause without which intellect would not exist, because they found an action like His in the witnessed world to be frivolous. And they obligated in the case of harmful actions if it were without benefit, that it follows folly, as the dualists mentioned concerning an action from which the agent does not benefit. Then they differed. A group claimed that there is no real harm on the one acted upon, even if from it is supplication and complaint. And a group claimed that there is real harm upon him, but he must compensate him for it, so that the action becomes wisdom, like what exists in the witnessed world: one who bears great burdens and drinks unpleasant medicines with intention, and intends taxation for outcomes, and he cannot harm others except with compensation.
Source pages p. 814

Commentary
This passage presents the claim of a group from among Ahl al-Tawhid (likely the Mu'tazila) who deviate from true tawhid in two ways: ignorance of what is obligatory for God, or inability to articulate the correct position against the dualists and atheists. They argue that a wise agent does not act without benefit or cause, so God, being wise, cannot initiate harm. Therefore they obligate al-aslah (the most beneficial) for others in religion and destiny, because God is self-sufficient. They limit God's actions to those that benefit or repel harm from others, making that the cause of His action, analogizing to human wise agents who act for benefit or to avoid harm. They illustrate by saying God cannot lie, be unjust, move without displacement, or be still without stability, so His actions must be estimated like those of wise people in the witnessed world, except that God is elevated above gaining or losing by action. Thus they conclude that God's actions are necessarily for the benefit or harm-repulsion of others, to avoid frivolity. They distinguish themselves from the dualists, who also require benefit to the agent, but the dualists explain wisdom through mixture (mizaj) and substance, whereas the people of tawhid oppose them on two points. Then these claimants differ among themselves: some say there is no real harm to the one acted upon (only perception of harm), while others say there is real harm but compensation is required, like bearing burdens or taking medicine for a good outcome, and one cannot harm without compensation. This sets up the position Maturidi will refute.

Key Terms
al-aslah (الأصلح)
'abath (عبث)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's actions are bound by the same moral obligations as humans.
Correction: God is transcendent and not subject to human standards of benefit or harm.

Checkpoint
According to the claimants, why must God's actions be for the benefit of others?
A) Because God is needy and seeks benefit for Himself.
B) Because they analogize God's wisdom to human wisdom, and a wise person only acts for benefit.
C) Because God cannot do harmful actions under any circumstances.
D) Because the dualists forced them to that conclusion.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite claim that God must act for the most beneficial outcome is based on an analogy to human wisdom and the rejection of purposeless action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a hardship that seems utterly pointless, does your heart secretly accuse God of being less than perfectly wise? Where does that accusation come from, and how does this lesson expose its root? Will you today surrender your need to see the benefit before you trust His wisdom?
?
The claimants measured God's actions by human standards of benefit. In what area of your life do you still expect God to act in a way that makes sense to you—by your definition of good? What would it cost you to abandon that expectation and submit to His absolute transcendence?
?
If God's actions are not bound by any necessity to benefit you, then your comfort, your plans, and your very existence are sustained by pure grace, not obligation. Does that thought make you anxious or does it fill you with awe? How will you live differently today knowing that every breath is a gift, not a debt?

Analogy to Human Wisdom: The Claimants' Argument from the Witnessed World
Maturidi presents the claimants' analogy and its implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the claimants use analogies from the witnessed world to argue that God's actions must be estimated on the model of wise humans.

Core Idea
The claimants use the witnessed world to claim that God's actions are like those of wise humans, except He gains nothing.

The claimants deepen their argument by drawing analogies from the witnessed world (al-shahid). They argue that just as a wise human cannot lie or act arbitrarily, God cannot act without benefit to others. They also exclude from God any elevation or abasement through action, concluding that His actions are purely for the benefit of others.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on analogy
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the examples they give: lying, injustice, motion without displacement, stillness without stability.
These are impossible for God, just as they are for a wise person.
2
Understand the necessity of analogy
They say it is necessary to estimate God's actions on the model of wise people in the witnessed world, but with the exception that God does not gain or lose by action.
This exception allows them to claim that God's actions are entirely for others.
3
Grasp the conclusion
The conclusion is that God's action must be wisdom by benefiting others or repelling harm, and that is the cause of His action to avoid frivolity.
This is the core of the al-aslah theory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Issue: God's actions. Regarding that a group from among the people of tawhid claimed that most of its adherents departed from it in two ways: either ignorance of what is obligatory for Him, or inability to summarize the statement about it from the school of the dualists and the rest of the atheists. So a group claimed that if every rational being acts without benefit [his action falls] then he is not wise, and whoever does an action without a cause is frivolous. So they thought that it is not permissible for God to initiate a harmful action against anyone, and that would remove wisdom from Him. So they obligated upon Him in every action He does the most beneficial for others in religion and the best for others in the final outcome; since He is exalted above a saying that benefits Him or harms Him. So they saw no action for Him except that which benefits others, or repels harm from others. That also becomes the cause of His action, just as is the cause of every wise person among us who considers immediate or delayed benefit or repels an incurred harm, thereby earning good praise and abundant reward. And they set an example for estimating His action by the action of others, including that lying or injustice cannot come from Him, nor motion without displacement, nor stillness without stability. So it was established that estimating His action on the model of wise people in the witnessed world is necessary, except that they removed from Him exaltation by action and abasement by leaving an action. So they thereby obligated that by His action He does not draw benefit to Himself nor repel harm from Himself, so His action must be wisdom by benefiting others or repelling harm from others. They made that the cause of His action, so that in their view His action would exit from the meaning of frivolity. And in this respect they opposed the dualists, since the dualists rejected that an action without benefit to the agent could be from wisdom. So the dualists affirmed action with the substance of wisdom at the time of mixture, so that in his salvation from the species of the substance of folly, his action becomes wisdom according to the estimation of the witnessed world: that something cannot come from nothing in the witnessed world. So the people of tawhid opposed them in these two points. Commentary

Checkpoint
What exception do the claimants make when comparing God's actions to those of wise humans?
A) That God can do what humans cannot.
B) That God does not gain elevation or abasement from action.
C) That God's actions are not bound by wisdom.
D) That God's actions are only for Himself.

The claimants' analogy from the witnessed world leads them to conclude that God's actions are necessarily for the benefit of others, as a requirement of wisdom and to avoid frivolity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that God's actions are purely for your benefit and not for His own, how does that reshape your response to hardships in your life? Are you willing to trust His wisdom even when it seems difficult?
?
The claimants argued that God's actions cannot be frivolous. Where in your own life have you doubted that God's actions have a purpose? What does this passage demand you repent from?
?
This passage shows the claimants making God's actions conditional on benefit to others. Do you ever act conditionally towards God, expecting something in return before obeying? How does this challenge your sincerity in worship?

Opposing Dualists and Internal Disagreements on Harm
Maturidi contrasts the claimants with dualists and notes their internal split.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the claimants distinguish themselves from dualists and then disagree among themselves about whether God's actions cause real harm and whether compensation is required.

Core Idea
The claimants oppose dualists on benefit but then disagree if harm is real or requires compensation.

Having established their view, the claimants contrast it with the dualist position. The dualists also require benefit to the agent, but they explain wisdom through mixture (mizaj) and substance. The people of tawhid reject this. Then the claimants themselves split: some deny real harm to the acted-upon, while others affirm harm but require compensation, like bearing burdens for a good outcome.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on dualists
Read the Arabic and translation about how the dualists require benefit to the agent and explain wisdom through mixture. Note the two points of opposition.
The dualists affirm action with the substance of wisdom at the time of mixture.
2
Understand the opposition
The people of tawhid oppose the dualists in two ways: regarding the necessity of benefit to the agent and the explanation via mixture.
This is a brief reference; details come later.
3
Examine the internal disagreement
Some claimants say no real harm exists (only perception), while others say harm is real but compensation is needed, like taking medicine or paying taxes with a good end.
This shows the early debate within the Mu'tazila.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة
أفعال الله
عن أن
زعم قوم من أهل التوحيد أن أكثر منتحليه خرج منه من وجهين: إما جهلا بواجبه، وإما عجزا عن تلخيص القول فيه من مذهب الثنوية وسائر الملحدين. فزعم قوم أنه إذ كان كل مما يعقل لغير نفع [فعله يقع] فليس بحكيم، ومن فعل فعلا لغير علة فهو عابث، فظنوا أن لا يجوز لله أن يبتدأ فعل ضرر بأحد، وأن ذلك يزيل الحكمة عنه، فألزموه في كل فعل يفعله الأصلح لغيره في الدين والأحسن لغيره في العاقبة؛ إذ هو متعال عن قول ينفعه أو يضره شيء، فلم يروا له الفعل إلا بما ينفع غيره، أو يدفع به الضرر عن غيره، فيكون ذلك أيضا علة فعله، على ما كان علة فعل كل حكيم منا، ما تأمل من نفع عاجل أو آجل أو دفع [ضرر] لزم به، فيجر بذلك حسن الثناء جزيل الثواب. وضربوا لتقدير فعله بفعل غيره مثلا بما لا يجوز أن يكون منه الكذب أو الجور، أو يكون منه الحركة [من] غير زوال، أو السكون [من] غير قرار، فثبت أن تقدير فعله على فعل الحكماء في الشاهد لازم، إلا أنهم دفعوا عنه الارتفاع بالفعل، والانحطاط بترك فعل ما، فأوجبوا بذلك أنه بفعله لا يجر إلى نفسه النفع ولا يدفع عنها الضرر، فيجب أن يكون فعله الحكمة بما ينفع غيره أو يدفع عن غيره الضرر، وجعلوا ذلك علة فعله؛ ليخرج عندهم فعله عن معنى العبث. وبهذا الوجه خالفوا الثنوية؛ إذ أبوا الفعل بغير نفع للفاعل فيه أن يكون من الحكمة، فأثبتوا الفعل بجوهر الحكمة عند المزاج، ليكون في خلاصه من جنس جوهر السفه، فيصير فعله حكمة على التقدير بالشاهد ما كون شيء لا من شيء ممتنعا في الشاهد، فأوجبوا لكلية العالم أصلا جعل وإنشاء؛ لأنه لا فصل بين خروج الفعل عن حق الوجود في الشاهد، فيلزم دفعه أن يكون ذلك من حكيم. فخالفهم أهل التوحيد في هذين، ثم ألزم فريق منهم إياه ما في العقل علة لم يكن له العقل دونها لما وجدوا فعل مثله في الشاهد عبثا، وألزموا في فعل المضار لو كان لغير نفع، يعقب سفها على ما ذكرت الثنوية في فعل لا ينتفع به الفاعل منه. ثم تفرقوا، فزعم قوم أنه لا ضرر في الحقيقة على المفعول به، وإن منه التضرع والشكوى. وزعم قوم أن عليه في الحقيقة ضررا، لكن عليه أن يعوضه عن ذلك؛ ليصير الفعل به حكمة، كالموجود في الشاهد ممن يحمل المؤن العظام وشرب الأدوية الكريهة مع القصد، وقصد الخراج لتقع العواقب، وليس له فعل الضار بغير إلا بعوض.
Issue: God's actions. Regarding that a group from among the people of tawhid claimed that most of its adherents departed from it in two ways: either ignorance of what is obligatory for Him, or inability to summarize the statement about it from the school of the dualists and the rest of the atheists. So a group claimed that if every rational being acts without benefit [his action falls] then he is not wise, and whoever does an action without a cause is frivolous. So they thought that it is not permissible for God to initiate a harmful action against anyone, and that would remove wisdom from Him. So they obligated upon Him in every action He does the most beneficial for others in religion and the best for others in the final outcome; since He is exalted above a saying that benefits Him or harms Him. So they saw no action for Him except that which benefits others, or repels harm from others. That also becomes the cause of His action, just as is the cause of every wise person among us who considers immediate or delayed benefit or repels an incurred harm, thereby earning good praise and abundant reward. And they set an example for estimating His action by the action of others, including that lying or injustice cannot come from Him, nor motion without displacement, nor stillness without stability. So it was established that estimating His action on the model of wise people in the witnessed world is necessary, except that they removed from Him exaltation by action and abasement by leaving an action. So they thereby obligated that by His action He does not draw benefit to Himself nor repel harm from Himself, so His action must be wisdom by benefiting others or repelling harm from others. They made that the cause of His action, so that in their view His action would exit from the meaning of frivolity. And in this respect they opposed the dualists, since the dualists rejected that an action without benefit to the agent could be from wisdom. So the dualists affirmed action with the substance of wisdom at the time of mixture, so that in his salvation from the species of the substance of folly, his action becomes wisdom according to the estimation of the witnessed world: that something cannot come from nothing in the witnessed world. So they obligated for the whole world an origin of creation and formation, because there is no distinction between the action exiting from the right of existence in the witnessed world, so it necessitates that it be from a wise [agent]. So the people of tawhid opposed them in these two points. Then a group among them obligated upon Him that in the intellect there is a cause without which intellect would not exist, because they found an action like His in the witnessed world to be frivolous. And they obligated in the case of harmful actions if it were without benefit, that it follows folly, as the dualists mentioned concerning an action from which the agent does not benefit. Then they differed. A group claimed that there is no real harm on the one acted upon, even if from it is supplication and complaint. And a group claimed that there is real harm upon him, but he must compensate him for it, so that the action becomes wisdom, like what exists in the witnessed world: one who bears great burdens and drinks unpleasant medicines with intention, and intends taxation for outcomes, and he cannot harm others except with compensation.
Source pages p. 814

Commentary
This passage presents the claim of a group from among Ahl al-Tawhid (likely the Mu'tazila) who deviate from true tawhid in two ways: ignorance of what is obligatory for God, or inability to articulate the correct position against the dualists and atheists. They argue that a wise agent does not act without benefit or cause, so God, being wise, cannot initiate harm. Therefore they obligate al-aslah (the most beneficial) for others in religion and destiny, because God is self-sufficient. They limit God's actions to those that benefit or repel harm from others, making that the cause of His action, analogizing to human wise agents who act for benefit or to avoid harm. They illustrate by saying God cannot lie, be unjust, move without displacement, or be still without stability, so His actions must be estimated like those of wise people in the witnessed world, except that God is elevated above gaining or losing by action. Thus they conclude that God's actions are necessarily for the benefit or harm-repulsion of others, to avoid frivolity. They distinguish themselves from the dualists, who also require benefit to the agent, but the dualists explain wisdom through mixture (mizaj) and substance, whereas the people of tawhid oppose them on two points. Then these claimants differ among themselves: some say there is no real harm to the one acted upon (only perception of harm), while others say there is real harm but compensation is required, like bearing burdens or taking medicine for a good outcome, and one cannot harm without compensation. This sets up the position Maturidi will refute.

Key Terms
thunawiyya (ثنوية)
mizaj (مزاج)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Mu'tazilites agreed on harm and compensation.
Correction: This passage shows early internal difference: some denied real harm, others affirmed it with compensation.

Checkpoint
What is the internal disagreement among the claimants regarding harmful actions?
A) Some say God cannot harm at all, others say He can but doesn't.
B) Some say no real harm exists, others say harm is real but requires compensation.
C) Some say harm is always compensated, others say it is not.
D) Some say harm is only in this world, others say in the afterlife.

Key Takeaway
The claimants distinguish themselves from dualists but then disagree internally on whether God's actions cause real harm and whether compensation is necessary for wisdom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience deep pain or loss, do you instinctively feel that God owes you something in return? How does the position that 'there is no real harm' challenge your immediate reaction, and can you sincerely embrace it?
?
Do you sometimes think God's actions must directly benefit Him to be wise? This passage shows even the dualists rejected that. Where in your heart do you hold God to human standards of wisdom?
?
If you believe God compensates every harm, how does that change your patience in suffering? Are you truly patient, or are you secretly tallying a debt you expect to be repaid?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
6 min
God's Wisdom Beyond Benefit
Maturidi refutes the claim that God's actions must benefit others.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that God's action cannot be constrained by the principle of benefit (al-aslah) and how he bases this on God's attributes of self-sufficiency and knowledge.

Core Idea
God’s actions are wise by essence, not by benefit.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi directly challenges the theological claim that God must always act for the optimal benefit of His creatures (al-aslah). He argues that such a view misunderstands God's nature. By establishing that God is wise by essence, free from ignorance and need, Maturidi shows that God's wisdom is not dependent on external benefits. This lesson unpacks his reasoning and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the ellipsis '..' indicating missing text, but the argument remains clear.
2
Identify the key attributes
Maturidi lists God's attributes as wise by essence, self-sufficient, and all-knowing. These form the foundation of his argument.
3
Understand the cause of unwisdom in creatures
In the witnessed world (al-shahid), departure from wisdom is caused by ignorance or need. This is a crucial premise.
4
Apply the negation to God
Since God is free from ignorance and need, His actions cannot depart from wisdom. This is the core inference.
5
Reflect on the motion/stillness analogy
Maturidi refutes analogies that compare God's actions to human actions involving motion or stillness, because these stem from need.
This reinforces the principle that God's actions are incomparable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ : من عرف الله حق المعرفة وعلم غناه وسلطانه ثم قدرته وملكه في أنه له الخلق والأمر عرف أن فعله لا يجوز أن يخرج عن الحكمة؛ إذ هو حكيم بذاته، غنى عليم، والذي به الخروج عن الحكمة في الشاهد ويبعث صاحبه عليه جهله أو حاجته، وهما منفيان عن الله، فثبت أن فعله غير خارج عن الحكمة. وعلى ما ذكرت يبطل أن يكون فعله في الحركة أو السكون؛ إذ .. هما حاجتان تحلان في صاحبها فيبلغه أحدهما إلى تأمل نفسه من الراحة والسلوى
The Shaykh said: Whoever knows God with true knowledge and knows His self-sufficiency and sovereignty, then His power and dominion, that to Him belongs creation and command, knows that His action cannot depart from wisdom; for He is wise by essence, self-sufficient, all-knowing. That which causes departure from wisdom in the witnessed world and drives its possessor to it is his ignorance or his need, and both are negated from God. So it is established that His action is not outside wisdom. And based on what was mentioned, it is invalid that His action be in motion or stillness; for .. they are two needs that settle in their possessor, and one of them brings him to contemplation of himself from rest and comfort.
Source pages p. 815

Commentary
This passage is Maturidi's refutation of the claim that God's actions must be for the benefit of others. He begins by stating a condition: whoever truly knows God—His self-sufficiency, sovereignty, power, and dominion—knows that His action cannot depart from wisdom. The reason is that God is wise (hakim) by essence (bi-dhatihi), self-sufficient (ghani), and all-knowing ('alim). In the witnessed world (al-shahid), departure from wisdom is caused either by ignorance or by need. Both ignorance and need are decisively negated from God. Therefore, God's action is necessarily within wisdom. Maturidi then applies this to the specific analogies used by the claimants: the examples of motion and stillness. Motion and stillness in creatures arise from need (e.g., need for rest or movement), but God is free from such needs, so it is invalid to compare God's actions to those of creatures in these respects. The passage concludes with an incomplete sentence (likely due to the manuscript break) about these needs leading to self-contemplation of rest and comfort, which further emphasizes that God is above such states.

Key Terms
الحكيم
غني
عليم
الشاهد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's wisdom is like human wisdom, based on beneficial outcomes.
Correction: Maturidi shows God's wisdom is intrinsic, not dependent on benefit, because God is self-sufficient and all-knowing, free from ignorance and need.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the ultimate proof that God's action is always wise?
A) God has infinite power.
B) God is wise by essence, self-sufficient, and all-knowing, so ignorance and need are impossible for Him.
C) The dualists also agree that God's actions are wise.
D) Creation itself shows wisdom, so God's actions must be wise.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi establishes that God's actions are necessarily wise because God is free from ignorance and need, thus refuting the doctrine of al-aslah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a trial where no good seems to come, do you find yourself doubting God's wisdom because you cannot see the benefit? How does knowing that God's wisdom is intrinsic—not dependent on your understanding or benefit—challenge your faith in that moment? Will you commit to trusting His wisdom regardless of your perception?
?
If God's actions are free from any need, including the need to please you, then what is the basis of your worship? Is it transactional—expecting something in return—or is it purely recognition of His glory? How would your prayer change if you truly believed God does not need your worship but is worthy of it?
?
Consider a time you felt God 'owed' you an explanation for suffering. Based on this lesson, God's actions are wise by essence, not by your approval. Will you repent of any expectation that God must justify Himself to you, and instead surrender your need to understand? What would that surrender look like practically?

Divine Attributes

Knowing God's Attributes Leads to Knowing His Actions Are Wise
Maturidi presents the conditional proof that knowledge of God's attributes necessitates wisdom in His actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that recognizing God's self-sufficiency, power, and sovereignty necessarily leads to the conclusion that His actions are wise, because ignorance and need—the causes of unwisdom—are absent in Him.

Core Idea
God's actions are wise because He is free from ignorance and need.

Maturidi begins by establishing a fundamental link between knowing God's attributes and recognizing the wisdom in His actions. He argues that anyone who truly understands God's self-sufficiency, authority, and power will inevitably see that His actions must be wise. This lesson unpacks that connection and shows why unwise actions are impossible for God.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the conditional structure: 'Whoever knows... knows that his action cannot exit from wisdom.'
2
Identify the two causes of unwisdom
The passage states that in the witnessed world, actions lack wisdom due to ignorance or need. Find this and note why both are negated from God.
3
Understand the conclusion
The passage concludes that God's actions are established as not exiting from wisdom. Ask yourself: why is this conclusion necessary given the premises?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ : من عرف الله حق المعرفة وعلم غناه وسلطانه ثم قدرته وملكه في أنه له الخلق والأمر عرف أن فعله لا يجوز أن يخرج عن الحكمة ؛ إذ هو حكيم بذاته ، غنى عليم ، والذى به الخروج عن الحكمة فى الشاهد ويبعث صاحبه عليه جهله أو حاجته ، وهما منفيان عن الله ، فثبت أن فعله غير خارج عن الحكمة . وعلى ما ذكرت يبطل أن يكون فعله فى الحركة أو السكون ؛ إذ هما حاجتان يُحلان فى صاحبها فيبلغه أحدهما إلى تأمل نفسه من الراحة والسلوى ، إلى ما يبلغه الهمة والرغبة ؛ إذ لا سبيل له إلى مقصوده إلا بالتحرك والزوال ، ولا إلى دفع الإعياء والتعب إلا بالقرار والسكون . فأما الله سبحانه إذ ثبت غناه وقدرته بطل أن يعتريه حاجة أو يعتريه همة . وعلى ذلك لما ثبتت قدرته وسلطانه وعلمه بطل وصفه بأن لا يقدر على فعل شيء ابتداء لا عن شيء ؛ إذ ذلك علم الحاجة وآية الضعف. وحاجة جميع ما يحس ويبلغه علم البشر هي الدلالة على تقدير العالم ، وعالم به قدير غنى ، لم يجز إزالة ذلك بالذي عرف غناه وقدرته وحكمته وعلمه ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . فلذلك لزم القول بضرورة العقل لجواز كون العالم لا عن شيء، وخروج فعله على الحكمة ، وإن عجزت عقول حكماء العالم عن إدراكها لخروج وجه الحكمة عن نهاية قوة عقولهم ، على ما بينا من كون شيء لا عن شيء ، ومن جواز فعل ممن لا ينتفع به ، وبذلك تظهر حقيقة الأمر له ، وأن له الخلق والأمر ، ولكل ذى ملك أن يفعل في ملكه على قدر ما ملك منه ما شاء ، ولا قوة إلا بالله
The Shaykh said: Whoever knows God with true knowledge and knows His self-sufficiency and authority, then His power and dominion, that to Him belong creation and command, knows that His action cannot exit from wisdom; for He is wise by His essence, self-sufficient, knowing. That by which exit from wisdom occurs in the witnessed world and impels its possessor to it is his ignorance or his need, and both are negated from God. So it is established that His action does not exit from wisdom. And according to what I have mentioned, it is invalid that His action be in motion or rest; for they are two needs that settle in their possessor, one bringing him to contemplation of himself from rest and consolation, to what aspiration and desire bring him; for there is no way to his goal except through movement and displacement, and no way to repel weariness and fatigue except through stillness and rest. As for God exalted, since His self-sufficiency and power are established, it is invalid that need or aspiration should befall Him. And likewise, when His power, authority, and knowledge are established, it is invalid to describe Him as not being able to do something initially from nothing; for that indicates need and is a sign of weakness. And the need of all that is sensed and attained by human knowledge is the indication of the ordainment of the world; and the world, with Him being powerful, self-sufficient, it is not permissible to remove that by what He knows of His self-sufficiency, power, wisdom, and knowledge. There is no power except with God. Therefore it is necessary to say, by necessity of reason, for the permissibility of the world's existence from nothing, and for His action to be upon wisdom, even if the intellects of the wise of the world are incapable of comprehending it because the aspect of wisdom exceeds the limit of their intellects' strength, according to what we explained of the existence of something from nothing, and of the permissibility of action by one who does not benefit from it, and by that the true nature of the matter becomes clear, that to Him belong creation and command, and every owner may act in his dominion according to what he possesses of it as he wills. There is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 815

Commentary
This passage is a proof (burhan) that God's actions are necessarily wise. Maturidi begins with a conditional: whoever truly knows God's attributes (self-sufficiency, authority, power, dominion) will know that His actions cannot lack wisdom. The reason is that in the witnessed world, actions lacking wisdom stem from ignorance or need—both absent in God. He then argues that God's actions are not like human actions of motion and rest, which arise from need (e.g., need to move to achieve a goal, need to rest to relieve fatigue). God is free from such needs. Since God's power, authority, and knowledge are established, it is invalid to claim He cannot create from nothing, as that would imply need and weakness. The ultimate conclusion is that reason necessitates acknowledging that the world can come from nothing and that God's actions are wise, even if human intellects cannot fully grasp the wisdom. This establishes God's absolute sovereignty: He does as He wills in His dominion.

Key Terms
حكمة
جهل
حاجة
الخلق والأمر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God might sometimes act unwisely or without purpose.
Correction: Maturidi argues that unwisdom stems from ignorance or need, both of which are negated from God. Therefore, all His actions are wise.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what two things cause actions to lack wisdom in the witnessed world?
A) Hatred and envy.
B) Ignorance and need.
C) Weakness and laziness.
D) Power and wealth.

Key Takeaway
True knowledge of God's attributes leads to the certain knowledge that His actions are always wise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly trust that every action of God in your life—including trials and hardships—is wise, even when you cannot see the wisdom? What would change in your heart if you lived with that certainty?
?
When you face a situation that seems unjust or pointless, do you subconsciously accuse God of ignorance or need? Examine your reaction: does it imply you think God lacks knowledge or has a need?
?
If God's actions are always wise by His essence, then your own suffering has a purpose. Are you willing to submit to that purpose without demanding an explanation? What is holding you back from that surrender?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
5 min
Why God's Actions Are Not Like Human Motion and Rest
Maturidi argues that God's actions cannot involve motion or rest because those imply need.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God's actions cannot be described as motion or rest because these imply need, which is incompatible with His self-sufficiency.

Core Idea
God is free from the needs that make motion and rest necessary for humans.

After establishing that God's actions are wise, Maturidi addresses a potential misunderstanding: that God's actions might involve motion or rest like human actions. He explains that motion and rest arise from need—to achieve a goal or relieve fatigue—and are therefore impossible for God, who is absolutely self-sufficient. This lesson explores that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the phrase 'يبطل أن يكون فعله فى الحركة أو السكون' - it is invalid for His action to be in motion or rest.
2
Identify the reasoning for motion/rest
The passage explains that motion and rest are 'two needs' that affect their possessor. Find the description of what motion and rest provide for humans.
3
Apply the reasoning to God
Since God's self-sufficiency and power are established, need and aspiration cannot befall Him. Understand why this negates motion and rest as attributes of His actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ : من عرف الله حق المعرفة وعلم غناه وسلطانه ثم قدرته وملكه في أنه له الخلق والأمر عرف أن فعله لا يجوز أن يخرج عن الحكمة ؛ إذ هو حكيم بذاته ، غنى عليم ، والذى به الخروج عن الحكمة فى الشاهد ويبعث صاحبه عليه جهله أو حاجته ، وهما منفيان عن الله ، فثبت أن فعله غير خارج عن الحكمة . وعلى ما ذكرت يبطل أن يكون فعله فى الحركة أو السكون ؛ إذ هما حاجتان يُحلان فى صاحبها فيبلغه أحدهما إلى تأمل نفسه من الراحة والسلوى ، إلى ما يبلغه الهمة والرغبة ؛ إذ لا سبيل له إلى مقصوده إلا بالتحرك والزوال ، ولا إلى دفع الإعياء والتعب إلا بالقرار والسكون . فأما الله سبحانه إذ ثبت غناه وقدرته بطل أن يعتريه حاجة أو يعتريه همة . وعلى ذلك لما ثبتت قدرته وسلطانه وعلمه بطل وصفه بأن لا يقدر على فعل شيء ابتداء لا عن شيء ؛ إذ ذلك علم الحاجة وآية الضعف. وحاجة جميع ما يحس ويبلغه علم البشر هي الدلالة على تقدير العالم ، وعالم به قدير غنى ، لم يجز إزالة ذلك بالذي عرف غناه وقدرته وحكمته وعلمه ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . فلذلك لزم القول بضرورة العقل لجواز كون العالم لا عن شيء، وخروج فعله على الحكمة ، وإن عجزت عقول حكماء العالم عن إدراكها لخروج وجه الحكمة عن نهاية قوة عقولهم ، على ما بينا من كون شيء لا عن شيء ، ومن جواز فعل ممن لا ينتفع به ، وبذلك تظهر حقيقة الأمر له ، وأن له الخلق والأمر ، ولكل ذى ملك أن يفعل في ملكه على قدر ما ملك منه ما شاء ، ولا قوة إلا بالله
The Shaykh said: Whoever knows God with true knowledge and knows His self-sufficiency and authority, then His power and dominion, that to Him belong creation and command, knows that His action cannot exit from wisdom; for He is wise by His essence, self-sufficient, knowing. That by which exit from wisdom occurs in the witnessed world and impels its possessor to it is his ignorance or his need, and both are negated from God. So it is established that His action does not exit from wisdom. And according to what I have mentioned, it is invalid that His action be in motion or rest; for they are two needs that settle in their possessor, one bringing him to contemplation of himself from rest and consolation, to what aspiration and desire bring him; for there is no way to his goal except through movement and displacement, and no way to repel weariness and fatigue except through stillness and rest. As for God exalted, since His self-sufficiency and power are established, it is invalid that need or aspiration should befall Him. And likewise, when His power, authority, and knowledge are established, it is invalid to describe Him as not being able to do something initially from nothing; for that indicates need and is a sign of weakness. And the need of all that is sensed and attained by human knowledge is the indication of the ordainment of the world; and the world, with Him being powerful, self-sufficient, it is not permissible to remove that by what He knows of His self-sufficiency, power, wisdom, and knowledge. There is no power except with God. Therefore it is necessary to say, by necessity of reason, for the permissibility of the world's existence from nothing, and for His action to be upon wisdom, even if the intellects of the wise of the world are incapable of comprehending it because the aspect of wisdom exceeds the limit of their intellects' strength, according to what we explained of the existence of something from nothing, and of the permissibility of action by one who does not benefit from it, and by that the true nature of the matter becomes clear, that to Him belong creation and command, and every owner may act in his dominion according to what he possesses of it as he wills. There is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 815

Commentary
This passage is a proof (burhan) that God's actions are necessarily wise. Maturidi begins with a conditional: whoever truly knows God's attributes (self-sufficiency, authority, power, dominion) will know that His actions cannot lack wisdom. The reason is that in the witnessed world, actions lacking wisdom stem from ignorance or need—both absent in God. He then argues that God's actions are not like human actions of motion and rest, which arise from need (e.g., need to move to achieve a goal, need to rest to relieve fatigue). God is free from such needs. Since God's power, authority, and knowledge are established, it is invalid to claim He cannot create from nothing, as that would imply need and weakness. The ultimate conclusion is that reason necessitates acknowledging that the world can come from nothing and that God's actions are wise, even if human intellects cannot fully grasp the wisdom. This establishes God's absolute sovereignty: He does as He wills in His dominion.

Key Terms
حركة
سكون
حاجة
همة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God 'moves' or 'rests' in a literal sense, as some anthropomorphists claim.
Correction: Maturidi argues that motion and rest are needs, incompatible with God's self-sufficiency, so they cannot apply to Him.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi say God's actions cannot be in motion or rest?
A) Because motion and rest are physical attributes.
B) Because motion and rest are needs that imply dependence.
C) Because God is unchanging.
D) Because the Quran does not mention them.

Key Takeaway
God's actions transcend the human needs that make motion and rest necessary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself rushing from one task to another, or collapsing in exhaustion, do you consciously remember that God is free from all such need? How does that truth change the way you view your own struggles?
?
This lesson teaches that God does not act out of any lack or goal to be attained. In what areas of your life have you been expecting God to 'move' or 'rest' like a human? How can you realign your expectations with His transcendence?
?
If God is self-sufficient and needs nothing from you, why do you still sometimes think your obedience or worship somehow adds to Him? How does this passage strip away any notion that God benefits from your actions?
