The Mu'tazila's Analogy: Denying Creation of Acts
Maturidi presents the Mu'tazila's principle and their analogy from substances to acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila's core argument that led them to deny that Allah creates human actions, based on their analogy from substances.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila deny creation of acts because they see no witnessed bringing from non-existence.

Maturidi begins by noting the principle of the Mu'tazila's denial. They argue that no one in the witnessed world brings something from non-existence to existence; at most, they combine and separate. By this analogy, they also deny that Allah creates human acts. Let's examine this reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Pay attention to the term 'Creator' and the principle of denial.
Notice how Maturidi contrasts 'Creator' with 'Speaker'.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila's principle
Locate the sentence that states the principle: the Mu'tazila deny creation because they find no action brought from non-existence to existence by another in the witnessed world.
This is the heart of their analogy.
3
Understand the analogy from substances
The Mu'tazila apply the same reasoning to acts as they do to substances: both involve only combining and separating, not true creation from nothing.
This analogy is weak according to Maturidi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا أن القول بالخالق يخرج مخرج التعظيم ، فكل ما هو أعم فهو أبلغ ، وبقائل لا ؛ لذلك اختلافا فنذكر معانى إنكاره أيضا . ثم الأصل أن انكار المعتزلة هذا بما لم يجدوا فعل أحد يخرجه غيره من العدم إلى الوجود ، وهو الأصل الذي له أنكر من أنكر خلق الأعيان بامتناعه فى الشاهد عن الوجود فى الحقيقة بفعل أحد ، بل فيه غير جمع وتفريق، فأبوا أن يكون خلق أعيان الأشياء بذلك ، وبمثله أنكرت المعتزلة خلق الأفعال ؛ فلذلك نسبهم الأوائل إلى ذلك ، مع ما قولهم في التحقيق ذلك ؛ لأنهم حققوا الأشياء في القدم، وجعلوا من الله ايجادها لا إحداث شيئيتها . وكانت الشيئية" لا به ، فيكون العالم عندهم في التحقيق حدثا أشياء ، لا أنه عن [۱۲۷] أحدث عن غير شيء ، ثم ذكروا فى الكفر / والإيمان أنهما شيئان ، كان الفاعل إيجادهما ، لا جعلها شيئين ، فصارا من حيث الشيئية ليس للعبد . ثم لا ينكر ذلك ، فما ينكر أن يكون من حيث الشيئية خلقا ، ولا يدفع ذلك ، ولم يوجب بذلك أنه عذب لا لشيء ، ولا أنه عذب للشيئية، ولا أحيل التعذيب إذا سقطت عنه الشيئية" ، ولا أوجب الشرك بين الفاعل والشيئية في العقل [و]فى الوجود ، ولا أطلق القول بأنه لإثنين ؛ إذ هو بكليته فى أنه شيء ليس له ، وفى أنه إيمان وكفر له ، وكذا هذا التقرير فى حركة المفلوج ، ولا قوة إلا بالله
And also that the expression 'Creator' comes out in the sense of glorification, so whatever is more general is more emphatic, and 'Speaker' is not; therefore they differ. So we mention the meanings of His denial as well. Then the principle is that the Mu'tazila's denial of this is because they did not find an action of anyone that is brought out by another from non-existence into existence, and this is the principle that caused whoever denied the creation of substances to deny it, due to its impossibility in the witnessed world of coming into existence in reality by the act of anyone, rather it involves only combining and separating. So they refused that the creation of the substances of things could be by that, and by the like of that the Mu'tazila denied the creation of acts. Therefore the early scholars attributed that to them, along with what their statement is in verification: that they verified things in pre-eternity, and made from Allah their bringing into existence, not the bringing about of their thingness. And thingness was not from Him, so the world became in their verification things that came into existence, not that it came from [something] brought into existence from nothing. Then they mentioned in kufr and iman that they are two things; the agent is the one who brings them into existence, not making them two things. So they become from the perspective of thingness not belonging to the servant. Then that is not denied. So what is denied is that from the perspective of thingness it is creation, and that is not repelled. And it does not necessitate by that that He punishes for no reason, nor that He punishes for thingness, nor is punishment impossible when thingness falls away, nor does it necessitate shirk between the agent and thingness in intellect and in existence, nor does it allow the statement that it is for two; because it in its entirety is something not belonging to him, and it is faith and kufr belonging to him. And likewise this determination in the movement of the paralyzed person, and there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 841

Commentary
This passage refutes the Mu'tazila's denial that Allah creates human acts. The author first notes that the term 'Creator' implies generality and glorification, unlike 'Speaker'. He then states the Mu'tazila's principle: they deny creation of acts because they analogize it to creation of substances, which in the witnessed world only involves combining and separating, not bringing from non-existence to existence. By this analogy, they also deny creation of acts. The author then explains their actual view: they affirm that Allah brings things into existence but not their 'thingness' (essence). This leads to the problem of faith and disbelief: they say faith and disbelief are two things that the servant acquires, but their thingness belongs to Allah? Actually the text says: 'the agent is the one who brings them into existence, not making them two things, so they become from the perspective of thingness not belonging to the servant.' This seems to say that the servant's action has thingness from Allah, but the actual quality (faith/kufr) is from the servant. The author then argues that this does not lead to absurdities like punishment without cause or shirk. He concludes with the example of the paralyzed person's movement.

Key Terms
خلق الأفعال
العيان
جمع وتفريق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila deny creation of acts because they believe humans create their own actions autonomously.
Correction: Maturidi shows their denial is actually based on an analogy from the empirical world, not a direct assertion of human power.

Checkpoint
What is the principle that the Mu'tazila use to deny that Allah creates human acts?
A) They find no one in the witnessed world who brings something from non-existence to existence.
B) They believe human acts are intrinsically good or evil.
C) They think Allah only creates substances, not accidents.
D) They affirm that humans are the sole creators of their acts.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila's denial of creation of acts stems from their analogy to substances, where no one brings something from non-existence to existence in the witnessed world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever attributed your good actions solely to your own power and choice, forgetting that Allah is the true Creator of every act, including your own? What specific action today can you consciously acknowledge as created by Allah, not just your own doing?
?
The Mu'tazila limited Allah's creative power based on what they observed. In what areas of your life do you implicitly limit Allah's power because you cannot see or understand how He works? What would it mean for you to trust in His absolute creation even when you cannot witness it?

Thingness (Shi'iyya) and Divine Creation
Maturidi explains the Mu'tazila's view on thingness and the world's origination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila's distinction between Allah's bringing into existence and the creation of thingness, and how this affects their view of the world.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila separate thingness from existence, attributing thingness to pre-eternity.

Maturidi explains the deeper basis of the Mu'tazila's position: they affirm that Allah brings things into existence, but they deny that He brings about their 'thingness' (essence). This leads to a world of pre-eternal things that come into existence from nothing. Let's examine this subtle distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, focusing on the terms 'thingness' and 'bringing into existence'.
The passage is short but dense.
2
Understand the concept of thingness
Thingness (shi'iyya) refers to the essence or quiddity of something, which the Mu'tazila consider pre-eternal and uncreated.
They distinguish between the existence and the essence of a thing.
3
Note the consequence for the world
According to this view, the world consists of pre-eternal things that become existent, not created from nothing (ex nihilo).
This is a key point of divergence from Sunni orthodoxy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

A) Their existence
B) Their thingness
C) Their accidents

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your own flaws or struggles, do you ever treat them as if they are 'pre-eternal' parts of you that Allah did not create and cannot change? How would your humility change if you truly believed that even your very essence is created by Allah at every moment?
?
The Mu'tazila limited Allah's creative act to bringing things into existence, not creating their nature. Are you aware of any area in your life where you implicitly believe that your 'nature' or 'personality' is fixed and beyond Allah's creative intervention? What would it mean to submit that area entirely to His creation?
?
If thingness is from Allah, then your identity, your thoughts, and your abilities are all constantly created by Him. Does this make you feel more dependent on Allah or more anxious? Why? What step can you take today to live out that dependence?

Faith and Disbelief: Thingness and Human Agency
Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazila's view on faith and disbelief using the thingness concept.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazila's view on faith and disbelief, and why it does not lead to absurdities.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila's distinction between thingness and quality makes faith and disbelief belong partly to Allah and partly to the servant.

Maturidi applies the Mu'tazila's thingness concept to faith and disbelief. They claim that the servant acquires the quality of faith or disbelief, but the thingness (essence) of these acts comes from Allah. Maturidi argues this does not imply punishment without cause or shirk. Let's examine his refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the words for faith (iman) and disbelief (kufr).
The passage contains several negations that Maturidi uses to refute possible consequences.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila's view on faith and disbelief
They say faith and disbelief are two things that the servant acquires, but their thingness (essence) is from Allah.
This makes the act belong to the servant in quality but not in thingness.
3
Understand Maturidi's refutation
Maturidi argues this does not lead to punishment without cause, shirk, or impossibility of punishment.
He also gives the example of a paralyzed person's movement to illustrate the point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

What does Maturidi argue is NOT necessitated by the Mu'tazila's view on thingness in faith and disbelief?
A) That the servant is the sole creator of his acts
B) That Allah punishes for no reason

D) That the world is created from nothing

Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazila by showing their own position on thingness does not lead to absurdities about punishment or shirk.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that your faith is a gift from Allah in its very existence, yet you are fully accountable for it? When you sin, do you secretly blame your nature or circumstances while forgetting that you chose the quality of that action?
?
If the thingness of your disbelief is created by Allah, does that make you resent Him? Or can you humbly accept that He creates the entity while you bear the responsibility for embracing it?
?
The paralyzed person's involuntary movement has thingness from Allah but no moral weight. What 'movements' in your life are you using as excuses, claiming they are just 'thingness'? Will you stand before Allah and say 'I could not help it' when the quality was yours to choose?

Divine Attributes

The Necessity of God's Exclusive Creation for Praise
Maturidi presents a rational argument that God's praise requires His exclusive creation of all things.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's rational argument that if any existent thing were not created by God, then praising Him would be either false or shared, thus requiring His exclusive creation of all things.

Core Idea
God's praise would be false if He did not create all things.

Maturidi begins with a profound logical point: the Qur'anic verses praising God for creating all things would be invalid if anything were excluded from His creation. In this lesson, we explore how he proves that God must be the sole Creator of everything, and what would happen if we allowed any exception.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow of the argument. Then read the English translation carefully.
Notice the logical structure: premise, then two hypothetical scenarios, then a reductio ad absurdum.
2
Identify the two problematic scenarios
Maturidi says if anything were excluded from God's creation, praising Him would be either for what is not His, or for something in which others share. Identify these two and understand why each is unacceptable.
The first leads to falsehood, the second to shirk in creation.
3
Understand the reductio argument
See how allowing exclusion leads to the conclusion that God is not the creator of anything, which is a description of blame.
4
Grasp the conclusion
The conclusion is that the only valid description is that God creates all things, which is praise and lordship. Specifying that He creates all affirms this.
This establishes tawhid in creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ رحمه الله : نقول وبالله التوفيق إذ ثبت أن الآية بحق الامتداح كان في خروج شيء من الكائنات امتداح بغير الذى له ، أو بما يشاركه فيه كل ضعيف ؛ لأنه لو أراد كلية الأشياء ، ولم يكن خلقها ، فامتدح بغير الذي له ، وذلك كذب ، وفى إخراج البعض مساواة غيره فى أنه صانع كل شيء ، يريد ما لا صنع لغيره فيه ، وذلك فاسد مع ما لو جاز ذلك على الصرف إلى غير الذي لغير فعل ليجوز أن يُقال : ليس بخالق شيء ، على أنه ليس بخالق ما هو فعل لغيره ، فاذ كان وصفا له بالذم والعبودة ثبت أن الأول وصف له بالمدح والربوبية ، وفى التخصيص إيجاب الأول . وأيضا أنه قال : هو رب كل شيء ، وإله كل شيء ، وهو على كل شيء وكيل ، ولم يجز إخراج شيء عن ذلك ، وإن كان لا يليق القول به على التخصيص لقبح نحو أن يقال : رب الخبائب وإله القبائح ووكيل الشياطين وابليس ، وقائم على كل نتن وقذر ، فمثله الأول : وإن كان يقبح على التخصيص فى أشياء من حيث التسمية . وبهذا الوجه الذي شهدت المجوس والزنادقة أن الله تعالى لم يخلق مؤذيا ولا فسادا ، ولا أمات وليا ولا قوني عدواً ، ولا أبقى الشياطين ، ولا أعطى من يعلم أنه يشتمه ويصد طاعته أحدا ، لقوة ذكرنا ذلك ليعلموا أن أصل الاعتزال مقدر عن ذلك ؛ إذ إليه فزعهم عند مخالفتهم المفهوم من القرآن ، ومما جرى عليه قول الإسلام. ولذلك قال رسول الله عليه السلام : القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة .
The Sheikh, may Allah have mercy on him, said: We say, and with Allah is success: Since it is established that the verse is for praise, if anything of existent things were to come out (of His creation), it would be praise for something not His, or for something in which every weak one shares with Him. For if He willed all things but did not create them, then He would be praised for what is not His, and that is false. And in excluding some (from His creation) is equating others with Him in that they are makers of everything, meaning what no one else has any act in, and that is corrupt. And if that were permissible regarding the directing (of acts) to other than the one who did the act, then it would be permissible to say: He is not the creator of anything, because He is not the creator of what is the act of another. Since it is a description of Him with blame and servitude, it is established that the first is a description of Him with praise and lordship, and in specification (making exclusive) is the affirmation of the first. And also He said: He is the Lord of everything, the God of everything, and He is over everything a guardian, and it is not permissible to exclude anything from that, even if it is not fitting to say it in specification due to ugliness, like saying: Lord of foul things, God of abominations, guardian of devils and Iblis, and one who stands over every filth and impurity. So similarly the first: even if it is ugly in specification regarding some things by way of naming. And by this aspect the Magians and Zoroastrians testified that Allah the Exalted did not create anything harmful nor corruption, nor did He cause the death of a saint nor strengthen an enemy, nor did He preserve the devils, nor did He give to one whom He knows will insult Him and obstruct His obedience anything, due to the strength (of their argument). We mentioned that so that they may know that the origin of Mu'tazilism is derived from that; for they resort to it when they contradict the understood meaning of the Qur'an and that which the saying of Islam proceeds upon. And for that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: The Qadariyya are the Magians of this community.
Source pages p. 843

Commentary
This passage is a proof from Maturidi arguing that God's praise for creating all things necessitates that He is the sole Creator of everything, and that excluding any existent from His creation would invalidate that praise and lead to false creed. He begins by establishing that the Qur'anic verse is for praise. If any thing were not created by God, then praising Him for it would be either praising Him for what is not His, or praising Him for something in which others share (since they would have created that thing). He then refutes the possibility that God willed all things but did not create them—this would be lying praise. Excluding some things from His creation also equates others with Him as makers of those things, which is corrupt. If it were allowed to attribute the act to one who did not do it, then one could say God is not the creator of anything, because He is not the creator of what others do. That would be a description of blame. Thus, the first description (that He creates all) is one of praise and lordship, and specifying that He creates all confirms that description. Maturidi then notes that God is described as Lord of everything, God of everything, and Guardian over everything, and none of this can be excluded even if it seems ugly to specify certain things like 'Lord of foul things'—the ugliness is only in the naming, not in the reality. He then points out that the Magians and Zoroastrians, due to this logic, denied that God creates harmful things, and that the Mu'tazilites took their origin from them. He ends with the hadith equating Qadariyya with Magians.

Key Terms
امتداح
إخراج البعض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God can be praised even if He did not create everything, as long as He created most things.
Correction: Maturidi argues that if any existent is excluded, praise becomes either false or shared, invalidating the praise. Therefore, God must create all things without exception.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, if any existent thing were excluded from God's creation, praising Him for it would be:
A) Acceptable because God is still the majority creator.
B) Either praise for what is not His or shared praise with others.
C) Acceptable if the thing is evil.
D) Impossible because God must create everything.

Key Takeaway
God's exclusive creation of all things is necessary for His praise to be true and unshared.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you achieve something significant, do you genuinely attribute the entire success to Allah's creation of that outcome, or do you secretly believe your own skill or effort played an independent role? How might this affect the sincerity of your gratitude?
?
Is there any area of your life—such as your health, wealth, or relationships—where you act as if the outcome depends on someone else's independent power, forgetting that Allah alone creates everything? What would change if you truly believed that no one else creates anything?
?
If you truly internalized that any praise of Allah for something He did not create would be false, would you still praise Him in times of hardship? Or would your praise be reserved only for the good you think He gave you? Examine your heart: do you praise Him even for difficulties, trusting that He alone created them for a purpose?

The Scriptural Proof and the Danger of Exclusion
Maturidi advances scriptural and theological arguments to forbid exclusion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses God's titles as Lord of everything and the ugliness of specifying certain things to argue against excluding anything from His creation, and how this connects to the Qadariyya deviation.

Core Idea
God's universal lordship leaves no room for excluding any creation from His authority.

Maturidi strengthens his argument by referencing God's description as Lord of everything and Guardian over everything, and then addresses the ugliness of specifying certain foul things. He then reveals that the Qadariyya and earlier heretics fell into error by excluding evil from God's creation, contradicting the clear meaning of the Qur'an.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the passage that begins with 'وأيضا أنه قال' to the end. Note the three divine titles mentioned.
The titles: Lord of everything, God of everything, Guardian over everything.
2
Understand the impossibility of exclusion
Maturidi argues that these titles cover everything, so excluding anything is impermissible. Even if specifying some things (like foul things) seems ugly, that is only in naming, not in reality.
3
See the sectarian connection
Maturidi points out that Magians and Zoroastrians denied God's creation of harmful things. This same logic led the Mu'tazilites to contradict the Qur'an.
The hadith equating Qadariyya to Magians reinforces this.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The lesson shows how a seemingly subtle exclusion leads to a major deviation. God creates all things, including what we consider foul or harmful.

قال الشيخ رحمه الله : نقول وبالله التوفيق إذ ثبت أن الآية بحق الامتداح كان في خروج شيء من الكائنات امتداح بغير الذى له ، أو بما يشاركه فيه كل ضعيف ؛ لأنه لو أراد كلية الأشياء ، ولم يكن خلقها ، فامتدح بغير الذي له ، وذلك كذب ، وفى إخراج البعض مساواة غيره فى أنه صانع كل شيء ، يريد ما لا صنع لغيره فيه ، وذلك فاسد مع ما لو جاز ذلك على الصرف إلى غير الذي لغير فعل ليجوز أن يُقال : ليس بخالق شيء ، على أنه ليس بخالق ما هو فعل لغيره ، فاذ كان وصفا له بالذم والعبودة ثبت أن الأول وصف له بالمدح والربوبية ، وفى التخصيص إيجاب الأول . وأيضا أنه قال : هو رب كل شيء ، وإله كل شيء ، وهو على كل شيء وكيل ، ولم يجز إخراج شيء عن ذلك ، وإن كان لا يليق القول به على التخصيص لقبح نحو أن يقال : رب الخبائب وإله القبائح ووكيل الشياطين وابليس ، وقائم على كل نتن وقذر ، فمثله الأول : وإن كان يقبح على التخصيص فى أشياء من حيث التسمية . وبهذا الوجه الذي شهدت المجوس والزنادقة أن الله تعالى لم يخلق مؤذيا ولا فسادا ، ولا أمات وليا ولا قوني عدواً ، ولا أبقى الشياطين ، ولا أعطى من يعلم أنه يشتمه ويصد طاعته أحدا ، لقوة ذكرنا ذلك ليعلموا أن أصل الاعتزال مقدر عن ذلك ؛ إذ إليه فزعهم عند مخالفتهم المفهوم من القرآن ، ومما جرى عليه قول الإسلام. ولذلك قال رسول الله عليه السلام : القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة .

Exclusion Invalidates Praise Due to Partners in Meaning
Maturidi argues that any exclusion from creation nullifies exclusive divine praise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that excluding anything from God's creation would nullify all exclusive praise for Him, because it would create partners in the reality of His attributes.

Core Idea
If creation is not exclusive, divine praise is not exclusive.

Maturidi presents a tight logical argument: if it were permissible for something to not be created by God, then the same permission would extend to His dominion, lordship, and all attributes of praise. This would mean that every attribute of God has partners in its true meaning, and thus no praise can be uniquely His. This passage shows the interdependence of God's creative power and His exclusive praise.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic text once without analysis. Notice the structure: a conditional statement followed by a conclusion.
The phrase 'ولا قوة إلا بالله' is a closing supplication, not part of the argument.
2
Understand the logical structure
The passage argues: if the exclusion of something from being created by God were allowed, then the same exclusion would apply to His dominion and lordship. This would mean partners share in the meaning of those attributes, so no praise is exclusive to God.
This is a reductio ad absurdum: the conclusion is unacceptable, so the premise is false.
3
Reflect on 'partners in the reality of its meaning'
Consider what 'partners in the reality of its meaning' entails. If something else shares in the reality of dominion, then dominion is not exclusive to God, and praise based on dominion is not unique to Him.
The argument shows the logical consequence of allowing any exception to God's exclusive creation.
4
Connect to Tawhid
This argument reinforces the Islamic doctrine of Tawhid: God is unique in His essence, attributes, and actions. Any compromise on His exclusive creation compromises all exclusive praise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو جاز خروج شيء من أن يكون يكون هو من أسماء له خالقا لجاز مثله عن الملك والربوبية ونحو ذلك الامتداح ، فيبطل أن يكون له مدح بشيء ؛ لما فى كل شيء له شركاء في حقيقة معناه ، ولا قوة إلا بالله .
And if the exclusion of anything from that He is (the one) from whose names [؟] He is Creator were permissible, then the like of that would be permissible regarding dominion, lordship, and similar praise, so that He would have no praise from anything; for in everything He has partners in the reality of its meaning. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 843

Commentary
This passage is a concise proof that excluding any entity from God's creation would logically lead to the collapse of all His exclusive attributes of praise. Maturidi argues that if it were allowed for something not to be created by God, then the same could be said for His dominion (al-mulk) and lordship (al-rububiyya)—others would share in those meanings. Consequently, no praise would be exclusively His because every attribute would have partners in its reality. The statement 'in everything He has partners' means that if creation is not exclusive, then dominion is not exclusive, etc., which is absurd. Thus, the original exclusion is invalid.

Key Terms
خروج
الملك
الربوبية
شركاء في حقيقة معناه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if some things are not created by God, then other attributes of God remain exclusive.
Correction: Maturidi shows that the same logic applies to all attributes: if creation is not exclusive, then dominion and lordship are also not exclusive, so no attribute is exclusively His.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi conclude would happen if exclusion of something from God's creation were allowed?
A) God would still have unique praise for other things.
B) God would have no exclusive praise because partners would share in the meaning.
C) The Magians would be correct.
D) The hadith would apply only to some.

Key Takeaway
If any being is excluded from God's creation, then all divine attributes lose exclusivity, and no praise is uniquely His.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If you truly believe that no being is independent of Allah, why do you sometimes act as if natural causes operate on their own? What would change in your daily life if you constantly acknowledged His exclusive creation in every event?
?
The argument shows that if even one thing is excluded from Allah’s creation, none of His praise remains exclusive. Is there any part of your life where you mentally reserve credit for yourself or others, thereby 'excluding' Allah? Are you willing to hand over that area entirely to Him?

Three Reasons Exclusion Is Invalid
Maturidi gives three proofs that excluding things from creation is invalid even if God is not mentioned in the name 'everything'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's three arguments against the claim that God's exclusion from the term 'everything' allows excluding creatures from His universal lordship.

Core Idea
God's universal attributes leave no room for excluding anything from His creation and lordship.

Maturidi addresses a subtle objection: if the term 'everything' in Quranic verses does not include God Himself, does that mean some creatures can be excluded? He finds this claim strange and provides three decisive proofs from the Quranic descriptions of God. This lesson walks through each reason step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the structure: a preliminary critique followed by three numbered reasons.
The passage uses technical terms like 'وكيل' and 'رب'.
2
Identify the three reasons
Look for the three reasons introduced by 'أحدها', 'والثاني', and 'والثالث'. Each reason is based on a different angle: universal attributes, nature of praise, and reference of lordship.
3
Understand the logic of each reason
For each reason, ask: How does it refute the idea that exclusion is permissible? Pay attention to how Maturidi uses Quranic phrases to show that universality is absolute.
The first reason uses universal guardianship and lordship; the second argues that inclusion would ruin the praise; the third shows that lordship implies a distinction between God and creatures.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
After studying the reasons, consider the overall message: God's attributes of power and lordship are all-encompassing, and no creature can be exempted from His authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله لم يدخل هو فيه عجيب . متى يذكر هو في اسم الأشياء بالإطلاق ، ولو جاز ذا الجاز أن يذكر في ذكر العلماء وذكر الفاعلين وذكر الوكلاء والأرباب ، وذلك كلام من لا يعتمل ما يقول . والملوك . وبعد ، فلو كان يذكر - وإن كان ممتنعا ذلك في العقل – الشيء لم يجز خروج غيره بخروجه لوجوه : أحدها قوله : وهو على كل شيء وكيل ، وهو رب كل شيء ، وإله كل شيء ، لم يجز خروج شيء من ذلك وتخصيصه في الخلق ليبطل معرفة المراد من حيث لم يدخل هو فيه . والثاني أنه امتداح ، وفى دخوله سقوطه ؛ إذ هو امتداح بما صير كل شيء تحت القدرة ، وحقق في كل العبودة ، وتحقيق ذلك فيه إبطال ذلك ، والله الموفق . والثالث أن القول المعروف بالفعل إلى آخر والربوبية ونحو ذلك راجع إلى ، وإذا كان كذلك فكأنه قال : سواى ، ولم يكن بمثله التخصيص ، فمثله الأول ، ولا قوة إلا بالله .
And his saying that He is not entered into it is strange. When is He mentioned in the name of things absolutely? And if that were permissible, then it would be permissible for Him to be mentioned among 'the learned' and 'the doers' and 'the agents' and 'the lords' and 'the kings', and that is the speech of one who does not consider what he says. And afterwards, if He were mentioned—even if that is impossible in reason—then it would not be permissible for something else to be excluded by His exclusion (from the name) for three reasons: One: His saying: 'And He is over everything a guardian, and He is the Lord of everything, and the God of everything', it is not permissible for anything to be excluded from that and to be specified in creation, for that would nullify the knowledge of the intended meaning, because He is not entered into it (the name 'everything'). Two: Because it is praise, and by His entry (into the name) the praise would be lost; for it is praise for making everything under power, and realizing in everything servitude, and actualizing that is nullifying it. And Allah is the giver of success. Three: Because the known saying regarding action to the end, and lordship and the like, refers back to Him. And if that is so, then it is as if He said: 'other than me', and specification would not be similar to that, so the same applies to the first. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 844

Commentary
This passage presents three arguments against the claim that since God is not included in the term 'everything' (i.e., 'everything' does not include God Himself), it is permissible to exclude certain creatures from His creation and lordship. Maturidi calls this claim strange. He points out that if God were to be included in the name of things absolutely, He would be mentioned among created beings like scholars, doers, agents, lords, and kings—which is absurd. Then he gives three reasons even if God were mentioned (in the name 'everything')—which is impossible in reason—exclusion of others would still not be permissible. First: The universal descriptions of God (Guardian, Lord, God of everything) do not admit exclusion of any created thing, and the fact that God Himself is not included in 'everything' does not affect the universal scope over creatures. Second: The praise of God for bringing everything under His power and realizing servitude in all creatures would be lost if He were included (as part of 'everything'), because then the praise would imply He has power over Himself, which is meaningless. Third: The known statements about action, lordship, etc., refer back to God, so they indicate a distinction between God and creatures. If God said 'everything except Me', that would allow specification, but He did not say that. Therefore, exclusion of creatures is invalid.

Key Terms
لم يدخل هو فيه
على كل شيء وكيل
رب كل شيء
امتداح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Since God is not included in the term 'everything', some creatures can be excluded from His universal lordship and creation.
Correction: God's universal attributes apply to all creatures without exception, and the verses are praise that would be invalidated if God were included.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi's second reason, why would including God in 'everything' nullify the praise?
A) Because praise requires the praised one to be separate from what is praised.
B) Because then God would be praising Himself for power over Himself, which is meaningless.
C) Because the verse would then refer to God alone.
D) Because the term 'everything' would become contradictory.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi demonstrates that God's universal attributes and the nature of praise leave no room for excluding any creature from His absolute sovereignty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as if God is the Guardian (وكيل) of every single aspect of your life, or do you secretly hold back some areas you think are outside His control?
?
The second reason says that the praise of God would be nullified if He were included in the term 'everything'. Reflect: Do you ever reduce God's majesty by imagining He is limited or comparable to creatures? How does this lesson correct that?
?
If all things are under God's power and lordship, then no part of your life is outside His authority. Is there an area you are trying to keep independent from Him? What would it mean for you to submit that area to Him today?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
6 min
God's creation of insult does not insult Him
Maturidi defends God from being associated with insult despite creating it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God's creation of the act of insult from a disbeliever does not make God insulted or blameworthy, according to Maturidi's reasoning.

Core Idea
God creates the act of insult as falsehood and injustice, which repels insult from Him.

Maturidi tackles a subtle objection: if God creates everything, including acts of evil, does that taint His holiness? He shows that the act of insult, when created by God, is not inherently insulting; its moral quality belongs to the creature. This passage defends divine transcendence and clarifies the relationship between God's creative act and the moral attributes of created actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get an overview of Maturidi's argument. Notice the flow from dismissing specification to the main objection and analogy.
2
Identify the objection addressed
Identify the core objection: if God creates everything, then He also creates the act of insult. Does that make Him insulted? Maturidi clarifies that no opponent claims God creates His own insult.
He distinguishes between creating an insult from a disbeliever and creating an insult directed at Himself.
3
Understand the key distinction
Maturidi argues that God creates the act of insult from the disbeliever as falsehood, injustice, and foolishness. These qualities actually repel insult and blame from God, because the act is created as a demonstration of the creature's disobedience.
The act as a created entity is neutral; its moral quality is in the creature's intention.
4
Analyze the analogy
Maturidi provides an analogy: a wise person knows the act of insult as a concept and is truthful, while a foolish person knows it as it is in the disbeliever and is ignorant. This illustrates that knowledge of the act does not make one participate in its moral blame.
5
Summarize the conclusion
The summary states that God's act of creation, considered as an accident or evidence of foolishness, is not described as insult or ugliness. Thus, creating the act does not impute insult to God.
This reinforces divine transcendence and the distinction between creator and creature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما ذكر من الآيات فقد بينا فساد الخصوص فى هذا ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . وما ذكر من الآيات، فقد بينا وشمه فيها ، وحصوله على الدعوى كهو فى هذا . وما ذكر نفسه وكفر به ونحو هذا ، فهو الذي لم يزل يعود نفسه من الذب على خصومه ، وليس أحد منهم يقول ذلك ، بل لو خلق شتم نفسه يكون مشتوما في الحقيقة مذموما ، بل خلق فعل الشتم من الكافر كذبا وجورا وسفها ، وفى ذلك دفع كونه مشتوما مذموما في الحقيقة . ألا أن تری من عرف فعل الشتم ؛ لذلك كان يكون عالما حكيما ، ومن أخبره عنه كذلك يكون صادقا ، ومن عرفه على ما عليه عند الكافر كان جاهلا سفيها ، وبالخبر بــه كذلك يكون كاذبا ، فمثله الذى ذكر ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . وجملته أن فعله من حيث كان عرضا أو شيئا أو دليلا على سفهه أو حركة ونحو ذلك لا يوصف بشتم ولا قبح ، فمثله من وجه خلقه إياه ، ولا قوة إلا بالله .
And what was mentioned of the verses, we have already shown the corruption of specification in this, and there is no power except with Allah. And what was mentioned of the verses, we have shown its meaning in them, and its conformity to the claim like what is in this. And what was mentioned of Himself and disbelief in Him and the like, that is what He has not ceased to defend Himself against his opponents, and not one of them says that. Rather, if He created the insult of Himself, He would be insulted in reality and blamed. Rather, He created the act of insult from the disbeliever as falsehood, injustice, and foolishness, and in that is the repelling of His being insulted and blamed in reality. Do you not see that whoever knows the act of insult is therefore knowledgeable and wise, and whoever informs about it likewise is truthful, and whoever knows it as it is in the disbeliever is ignorant and foolish, and by informing about it likewise he would be a liar. So the same applies to what was mentioned, and there is no power except with Allah. And the summary is that His act, insofar as it is an accident or a thing or an evidence of his foolishness or a movement and the like, is not described as insult nor ugliness, so the same applies from the aspect that He created it. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 844

Commentary
This passage addresses a potential objection: if God creates everything, including the act of insult (shutm) by a disbeliever, does that make God insulted or blameworthy? Maturidi first reiterates that he has already shown the fallacy of specifying exceptions in previous discussions. He then clarifies regarding objections about God creating His own insult and disbelief. He says no opponent actually claims that God created His own insult (i.e., that God creates an insult directed at Himself). Rather, God creates the act of insult from the disbeliever as an act of falsehood, injustice, and foolishness. This very act being falsehood etc. actually repels the notion that God is insulted or blamed. Maturidi draws an analogy: a person who truly knows the nature of the act of insult is wise and truthful; but one who knows it as it is in the disbeliever (i.e., as a foul act) would be ignorant and foolish if he attributes that to God. So God's act (of creating that act) is not described as insult or ugliness because it is an accident (arad), a thing, an evidence of the disbeliever's foolishness, etc. Therefore, from the aspect that God created it, it is not insulting or ugly. The key is distinguishing between the act as a created entity (which is neutral) and its moral quality that belongs to the creature.

Key Terms
خلق فعل الشتم
مشتوما مذموما
عرضا
دليلا على سفهه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God creates an evil act like insult, then God becomes insulted or blameworthy.
Correction: Maturidi argues that the act as created is neutral; its moral quality comes from the creature's intention and disobedience, not from God's act of creation.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why does God creating the act of insult from a disbeliever not make God insulted?
A) Because the act is not really an insult.
B) Because the act is created as falsehood and injustice, which repels insult from God.
C) Because God only creates good things.
D) Because the disbeliever is actually praising God.

Key Takeaway
God's creation of an act does not make Him share in its moral quality; the act is created as a neutral entity, and its blameworthiness belongs to the creature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a trial or injustice in your life, is your first reaction to blame God? How does Maturidi's teaching that God creates acts as neutral (with blameworthiness from the creature) confront your impulse to accuse Him? What specific step can you take today to redirect that blame toward your own accountability?
?
Think of a time you have been deeply hurt by someone else's insult or sin. Do you secretly hold God responsible for allowing that to happen? This lesson says that God creates the act with qualities that repulse insult from Himself—does that change how you view God's role in that painful event? Would you be willing to release your resentment toward God and instead see the creature's choice as the source of the harm?
?
Maturidi emphasizes that God is not insulted by creating the act. But are there areas in your own life where you feel that God's actions toward you have been insulting, unfair, or beneath His dignity? What would it mean for you to accept that God's creation of your circumstances—even the difficult ones—does not detract from His perfection, and that your real struggle is with your own reaction? What commitment will you make to honor His transcendence in your complaint?

Three Arguments Against Including God in Names
Maturidi presents three logical arguments against including God in created names.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three rational arguments Maturidi uses to prove that God cannot be included in the names of created things.

Core Idea
God cannot be encompassed by any created name.

Maturidi refutes a peculiar claim: that God could be included in the names of created things. He considers this absurd and provides three logical reasons to show why. This passage establishes a key principle of divine transcendence: Allah is not to be compared or mixed with His creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the three numbered arguments (وجوه).
Maturidi begins by calling the claim strange.
2
Analyze the first argument
The first argument: God is trustee, Lord, and God of everything, so nothing can be excluded from His dominion. Particularizing something would nullify the meaning.
This relies on Qur'anic descriptions.
3
Analyze the second argument
The second argument: Inclusion of God in names is praise, but His entry would cause the praise to fall because praise is for making everything under power.
Inclusion would contradict the praise.
4
Analyze the third argument
The third argument: Actions and lordship revert to God, so any statement implying 'other than me' is invalid. Particularization cannot apply to Him.
This mirrors the first argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله لم يدخل هو فيه عجيب . متى يذكر هو في اسم الأشياء بالإطلاق ، ولو جاز ذا الجاز أن يذكر في ذكر العلماء وذكر الفاعلين وذكر الوكلاء والأرباب ، وذلك كلام من لا يعتمل ما يقول . والملوك وبعد ، فلو كان يذكر - وإن كان ممتنعا ذلك في العقل – الشيء لم يجز خروج غيره بخروجه لوجوه : أحدها قوله : وهو على كل شيء وكيل ، وهو رب كل شيء ، وإله كل شيء ، لم يجز خروج شيء من ذلك وتخصيصه في الخلق ليبطل معرفة المراد من حيث لم يدخل هو فيه . والثاني أنه امتداح ، وفى دخوله سقوطه ؛ إذ هو امتداح بما صير كل شيء تحت القدرة ، وحقق في كل العبودة ، وتحقيق ذلك فيه إبطال ذلك ، والله الموفق . والثالث أن القول المعروف بالفعل إلى آخر والربوبية ونحو ذلك راجع إلى ، وإذا كان كذلك فكأنه قال : سواى ، ولم يكن بمثله التخصيص ، فمثله الأول ، ولا قوة إلا بالله .
And His saying 'He is not entered into it' is strange. When is He mentioned in the absolute naming of things? And if this were permissible, that He be mentioned in the mention of scholars, agents, deputies, and lords—that is the speech of one who does not consider what he says. And the kings? Then after, if He were mentioned—though that is impossible in reason—the thing would not permit the exclusion of other than Him by its exclusion, for aspects: first, His saying: He is the trustee over everything, Lord of everything, God of everything, it is not permissible for anything of that to be excluded and particularized in creation to nullify the knowledge of the intended meaning from where He is not entered into it. Second, it is praise, and His entry would be its fall; for it is praise for making everything under power, and realizing in all servitude, and realizing that nullifies it—and God is the giver of success. Third, the statement known by the action to the end, and lordship and the like, returns to Him; and if it is so, it is as if He said 'other than me', and particularization is not like that; so it is like the first—and there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 844

Commentary
This passage is a refutation presenting three logical arguments (وجوه) against the idea that God can be included in the names of created things. The author begins by deeming the claim strange, questioning how the absolute naming of things could include God. He then introduces three reasons: (1) First, because God is the trustee over everything, Lord, and God of all, nothing can be excluded from His dominion; particularizing something in creation would nullify the intended meaning of His encompassing authority. (2) Second, the supposed inclusion is a form of praise, but including God in it would actually nullify the praise, because the praise stems from Him having made everything subject to power and servitude; actualizing that inclusion would contradict the praise. (3) Third, the attribution of actions and lordship ultimately reverts to God, so any statement implying 'other than me' is invalid; particularization cannot apply to Him. The argument concludes by emphasizing that there is no power except through God.

Key Terms
وجوه
امتداح
تخصيص
وكيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is possible to include God in the names of created beings, or to say God is like a scholar, agent, lord, etc.
Correction: Maturidi argues that God is absolutely transcendent and cannot be included in any created name because it would contradict His unique attributes of being the Lord, Trustee, and God of all, and would nullify the praise due to Him.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the second argument (الوجه الثاني) against including God in names?
A) It nullifies knowledge of the intended meaning.
B) It would cause the praise to fall because praise is for making everything under power.
C) It implies God is like other things.
D) It is impossible in reason.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi's three arguments establish that God is utterly transcendent and cannot be included in any category of created names.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you use words like 'lord' or 'master' for anyone or anything in your life, are you ever tempted to think of God as just a bigger version of that title? How does Maturidi's second argument—that including God nullifies the praise—expose the error in that assumption? What concrete step can you take today to mentally separate God's lordship from all earthly authority?
?
You often refer to God as 'the Lord of everything' in your prayers. But do you truly live as if nothing is outside His dominion—including your time, your plans, your relationships? Where in your daily routine do you act as if something is 'excluded' from His authority? What would change if you took the first argument literally?
?
Maturidi says that any statement implying 'other than me' regarding God's actions is invalid. When you proudly say 'I did this' or 'I achieved that', do you realize you are implying that some action originates from other than God? How can you rephrase your thoughts and speech to reflect that all actions return to Him?

Four Aspects of Divine Praise and Refutation of Mu'tazila
Maturidi details four aspects of divine praise and refutes Mu'tazila claims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four aspects through which true praise of God is established, and how Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazila's flawed attribution of praise.

Core Idea
God's praise is unique, rooted in His absolute power and independence from creation.

In this passage, Imam al-Maturidi delves into the nature of divine praise, arguing that true praise stems from specific aspects that highlight God's sovereignty and the creature's utter dependence. He also critiques the Mu'tazila for attributing praise to God in a manner that compromises His transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation carefully to get an overview of the argument.
Notice the refutation of the Mu'tazila at the beginning.
2
Identify the four aspects of praise
Look for the four 'وجوه' (aspects) that Maturidi lists. Understand each one's basis in God's attributes.
The list starts with 'أحدها' (first) and continues.
3
Understand the refutation of Mu'tazila
See how Maturidi counters the Mu'tazila claim that praise can be attributed to God based on His creation.
Focus on the final part about the instability of that attribution.
4
Reflect on God's transcendence
Consider the conclusion that God's glory is permanent and free from interruption, unlike created praise.
5
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to see if you grasped the fourth aspect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعد، فإن الآية لو نزلت فيهم لنزلت في ذمهم ، ووصف فيما نفوا عن الله من الوجه الذي نفى أهل الاعتزال ، فذلك لازم لهم ، مع أن الآية لا يعمل بها المعتزلة من ذلك الوجه الذى فى أصل دينهم جواز إضافة حقيقة ذلك إلى الله ، فكيف يجتمع على منكر مثله ممن يزعم أن ذلك في العقل مدفوع ، وطريقة السمع . ومحال الاحتجاج بالسمع على إمكانه فى العقل ، ثبت أن حقيقة ذلك في أفعال الخلق ، وبه يكون امتداح فى الحقيقة من وجوه : أحدها في جعل كل شيء بحيث القدرة تحت قدرة الله ؛ ليظهر حاجة الخلق جملة إلى الله تعالى في كون كل شيء لهم به . والثانى أن الوصف بالقدرة على ما لا فعل لغيره ليس بعجيب ، بل يستحقه كل ضعيف مهان ، ثبت أن الامتداح يكون من هذا الوجه . والثالث فيه بيان سفه من يفهم أن خلف كل شيء على ما عليه يوجب وصف الرب ، أو تحقيق الفعل من الوجه الذى يكون من العباد منه . والرابع ليعلم أن الله يتعالى أن يلحقه ذم فى فعل أو مدح من حيث ذلك المفعول بحال ، وذلك ببعض الاعتزال ؛ إذ جعلوا له هذا الامتداح بخلقه ، وما يكون كذلك فهو شرف الدوام وخوف الانقطاع ، جل ربنا عن ذلك .
And then, if the verse had been revealed concerning them, it would have been revealed in their blame, and a description of what they denied about God from the aspect that the people of i'tizal denied; so that is binding upon them, even though the Mu'tazila do not act upon the verse from that aspect because in their religion it is permissible to attribute the reality of that to God. So how can one who denies such a thing—who claims that it is repudiated in reason and the method of transmission—agree? And it is impossible to argue by transmission for its possibility in reason. It is established that the reality of that is in the actions of creatures, and thereby praise is in reality from aspects: first, in making everything so that power is under the power of God, to show the need of all creatures towards God Almighty in the existence of everything for them. Second, describing with power over what no other can do is not wonderful, rather every weak and despised person deserves it, so it is established that praise arises from this aspect. Third, it contains an explanation of the foolishness of one who thinks that everything being as it is necessitates a description of the Lord, or the realization of the action from the aspect that it is from servants. Fourth, to know that God is exalted above being subject to blame in an action or praise from the aspect of that object in any state; and that is in some of the Mu'tazila, for they attributed this praise to Him through His creation, and what is like that is the honor of permanence and the fear of cessation—our Lord is exalted above that.
Source pages p. 845

Commentary
This passage is a refutation and classification. Maturidi argues that if a particular verse had been revealed against the Mu'tazila, it would have condemned them. He points out that the Mu'tazila themselves do not act on certain verses because their doctrine permits attributing reality to God, which is inconsistent. He then establishes that true praise of God consists in four aspects: (1) Making everything subject to God's power to show creation's need. (2) Describing God with power over what no other can do—even a weak person can claim power over his own actions, so this praise is unique. (3) Exposing the foolishness of those who think that the state of things necessitates describing God in human terms. (4) God is beyond any blame or praise based on the mere object of action; the Mu'tazila wrongly attribute praise to God based solely on His creation, which is unstable. Maturidi concludes that true glory is permanent and cannot be interrupted.

Key Terms
امتداح
قدرة
اعتزال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God's power is like human power.
Correction: Maturidi shows that God's power is absolutely unique: He has power over all things, whereas even a weak person can claim power over his own actions. True divine praise is based on His exclusive power and independence, not on any resemblance to creatures.

Checkpoint
According to the fourth aspect of praise (الوجه الرابع), what does Maturidi say about God's relation to praise and blame?
A) God is subject to praise based on His actions.
B) God is exalted above any blame or praise based on the object of action.
C) God's praise depends on His creation.
D) God's attributes are like those of creatures.

Key Takeaway
True praise of God is based on His absolute power and the perpetual need of all creation, not on any attribute resembling creatures.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you praise God, do you ever catch yourself praising Him for what He has given you rather than for who He is in Himself? This lesson teaches that true praise is rooted in His absolute power and your complete need. Before your next prayer, pause and recite 'Alhamdulillah' while intentionally detaching it from any blessing you've received—focus solely on His perfection.
?
The Mu'tazila thought God's glory depends on His creation. In your own life, do you ever feel that your acts of worship add something to God? How would your heart change if you deeply believed that He is exalted above any increase or decrease from your obedience? Commit today to perform one good deed purely to acknowledge His transcendence, not to seek any return.

The Four Aspects of Divine Praise in Creation
Maturidi enumerates four aspects of divine praise through creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four aspects through which God's praise arises from His creation, according to Imam Maturidi.

Core Idea
God's praise comes from His making all things dependent on Him, not from sheer power.

Imam Maturidi begins by establishing that revealed evidence cannot be used to prove what reason deems impossible. He then asserts that the true basis for praising God lies in His actions of creation. From this, he derives four distinct aspects of praise, each highlighting a different dimension of God's majesty and refuting misguided views.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: a principle followed by an enumeration of four aspects.
The passage is dense; read it slowly.
2
Identify the four aspects
Find the four numbered aspects (أحدها, الثاني, الثالث, الرابع). Understand each one's main point.
3
Connect each aspect to the central idea
Ask how each aspect shows God's praise is rooted in making creation dependent on Him.
This helps see the unity of Maturidi's argument.
4
Reflect on the refutation of Mu'tazila
In the fourth aspect, Maturidi explicitly criticizes the Mu'tazila. Understand why their view is problematic.
He says their view implies temporality and cessation, which is impossible for God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومحال الاحتجاج بالسمع على إمكانه في العقل، ثبت أن حقيقة ذلك في أفعال الخلق، وبه يكون امتداح في الحقيقة من وجوه: أحدها في جعل كل شيء بحيث القدرة تحت قدرة الله؛ ليظهر حاجة الخلق جملة إلى الله تعالى في كون كل شيء لهم به. والثاني أن الوصف بالقدرة على ما لا فعل لغيره ليس بعجيب، بل يستحقه كل ضعيف مهان، ثبت أن الامتداح يكون من هذا الوجه. والثالث فيه بيان سفه من يفهم أن خلف كل شيء على ما عليه يوجب وصف الرب، أو تحقيق الفعل من الوجه الذي يكون من العباد منه. والرابع ليعلم أن الله يتعالى أن يلحقه ذم في فعل أو مدح من حيث ذلك المفعول بحال، وذلك ببعض الاعتزال؛ إذ جعلوا له هذا الامتداح بخلقه، وما يكون كذلك فهو شرف الدوام وخوف الانقطاع، جل ربنا عن ذلك.
And it is impossible to argue by revelation (sam') for its possibility in reason. It is established that the reality of that is in the actions of creation, and by it there is praise in reality from aspects: One: in making everything such that power is under the power of God, to show the need of all creation to God Almighty in that everything is for them. The second: that the description of power over what no other does is not marvelous, rather every weak and contemptible one deserves it; it is established that the praise is from this aspect. The third: in it is an explanation of the foolishness of one who understands that the succession of everything as it is necessitates describing the Lord, or the actualization of the action from the aspect that is from servants. The fourth: to know that God is exalted above being subject to blame in an action or praise from that object in any state, and that by some of the Mu'tazila; for they made this praise for Him by His creation, and whatever is like that is the honor of permanence and fear of cessation, exalted is our Lord above that.
Source pages p. 845

Commentary
This passage is a proof and enumeration. Maturidi first states a fundamental principle: it is impossible to use revealed evidence (sam') to prove the rational possibility of something that reason deems impossible. He then asserts that the true reality of the matter under discussion lies in the actions of creation. From this, praise (imtidaah) of God arises in four aspects. First aspect: God's making everything dependent on His power, so that all creation's need for Him is manifest. Second aspect: having power over what no one else does is not remarkable; even the weakest being has power over its own actions, so true praise must come from something else. Third aspect: it shows the foolishness of thinking that the succession of events obligates describing God in a certain way or that actions are actualized from the same aspect as human actions. Fourth aspect: it makes known that God is far above being praised or blamed based on the object of the action; the Mu'tazila mistakenly attribute this kind of praise to God through His creation, but that would imply permanence and fear of cessation, which is impossible for God. Thus, Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazila position.

Key Terms
السمع
العقل
امتداح
أفعال الخلق
القدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God's praise comes from His sheer power alone, independent of creation.
Correction: Maturidi shows that true praise arises from making all creation dependent on Him, not from mere power.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the first aspect of praise from the actions of creation?
A) God's power over all things
B) God's making everything dependent on His power to show creation's need
C) God's creation of evil
D) God's independence from creation

Key Takeaway
God's true praise arises from His making all creation dependent on Him, not from mere power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself praising God only when you see impressive displays of power, while ignoring the subtle ways He makes everything dependent on Him? How can you shift your perspective to see His praise in your daily needs?

?
The Mu'tazila mistakenly thought God's praise comes from His creation in a way that implies fear of cessation. Are there moments when you fear that God's praise or your relationship with Him could end? How does this lesson call you to trust in His eternal nature?

Refutation of the Interpretation of 'Allah created you and what you do'
Maturidi refutes the opponent's proof from the verse and clarifies its meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi insists that the apparent meaning of 'what you do' in verse 37:96 refers to the creation of actions themselves, not the objects of those actions.

Core Idea
The verse creates actions, not objects—a key distinction in refuting anthropomorphic interpretations.

Imam Maturidi now tackles a critical proof used by opponents who interpret 'what you do' as referring to the idols or objects of human actions. By analyzing the verse's apparent meaning and parallel Quranic passages, he shows that the text is about the creation of the very act of doing, not the things made. This distinction is essential for preserving the uniqueness of divine creative power.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get the flow of the argument. Notice that Maturidi presents the opponent's view before his own refutation.
The passage ends mid-sentence; we only have the beginning of Maturidi's second point.
2
Identify the opponent's proof
The opponent uses verse 37:96 and parallels like 37:95 and 20:69 to argue that 'what you do' means the carved idols. Understand this claim.
3
Analyze Maturidi's first response
Maturidi says the apparent meaning (zaahir) of the verse is creation of the action (خلق العمل). He argues that it cannot be diverted to another meaning without evidence.
He also notes that the blame is on the action of carving, not the carved object.
4
Understand the second argument
Maturidi adds a logical point: if the verse is interpreted as creating objects (ma'mool), then if God did not create the action, one cannot say He created the object as a product of that action.
This part is incomplete but the logic is clear.
5
Reflect on the misconception
Consider the common misunderstanding that 'what you do' refers to idols. Maturidi corrects this by insisting on the literal sense of creating the act itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم احتج لخصمه بقوله: والله خلقكم وما تعملون، قال: يريد به، كقوله: (أتعبدون ما تنحتون)، وكقوله: (تلقف ما يأفكون). قال الشيخ رحمه الله: نقول وبالله التوفيق ظاهر الآية ذكر خلق العمل، فلم يجز صرف ذلك إلى غيره إلا بالبيان، مع ما في جميع ما ذكر نحتهم داخل، وكذلك إفكهم ما ذكر وبه عوبوا لا بذلك الشيء حيث فعلوا ثم عبدوا، فكأنهم عبدوا فعلهم فمثله ما نحن فيه. أيضا أنه لو شرح بالآية آلهتهم ذكر معمولا، فإذا لم يكن الله خلق العمل لم يجز له القول بخلقه معمولا؛ إذ
Then he argued for his opponent by His statement: 'And Allah created you and what you do.' He said: He means by it, like His statement: 'Do you worship what you carve?' and like His statement: 'It swallows what they faked.' The Shaykh, may God have mercy on him, said: We say, and with God is success: the apparent meaning of the verse mentions the creation of the action, so it is not permissible to divert that to other than it except by evidence. And with that, all that is mentioned of their carving is included, and likewise their faking, as mentioned, and by it they were reviled, not by that thing where they did then worshipped. So it is as if they worshipped their own action, so similar is what we are in. Also, if he explained by the verse that their gods are mentioned as an object, then if God did not create the action, it is not permissible for him to say that He created it as an object; because...
Source pages p. 846

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. Maturidi presents the opponent's proof from the Quranic verse 'Allah created you and what you do' (37:96). The opponent claims that 'what you do' refers to the objects of actions, i.e., the idols they worshipped. Then the Shaykh (Maturidi) responds. He says the apparent meaning (zaahir) of the verse is the creation of the action itself ('amal), not the object. Therefore, it cannot be turned away from that meaning without clear evidence. He then argues that all the things mentioned, such as their carving and faking, are included, but the blame is on the action of carving, not on the carved object. They worshipped their own actions, similar to the issue at hand. Then he adds another point: if someone interprets the verse to mean that the gods are the created objects (ma'mool), then if God did not create the action, it would not be permissible to say He created the object as a product of the action, because that would imply creation of the action itself. The passage ends mid-sentence, probably continuing the refutation.

Key Terms
ظاهر الآية
خلق العمل
المعمول
عبادة الفعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'what you do' refers to the idols that people worship, making God the creator of those objects.
Correction: Maturidi shows that the apparent meaning is creation of the action itself; the parallel verses blame the action, not the object.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the apparent meaning of 'what you do' in the verse?
A) The objects that are made
B) The actions themselves
C) The intentions
D) The materials used

Key Takeaway
Maturidi insists that 'what you do' refers to the creation of human actions, not the objects, preserving the doctrine that God creates all actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the verse 'Allah created you and what you do,' do you truly internalize that your every action—even your intention to obey—is created by Allah? How does this awareness challenge your sense of self-reliance when you perform good deeds?
?
The polytheists were condemned because they worshipped their own actions (carving). In what ways do you secretly admire or take pride in your own religious practices, forgetting that the ability and action itself come from Allah? What is one specific act of worship you need to consciously attribute back to Him?
?
Maturidi insists on adhering to the apparent meaning of the Quran unless clear evidence demands otherwise. Where in your life have you twisted a Quranic verse to suit your desires—like reinterpreting a command to make it easier? Will you repent and commit to accepting the apparent meaning, even when it is hard?

The Absurdity of Independent Human Power
Maturidi refutes independent human power via reductio.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why attributing independent power to humans implies they could thwart God's plans, leading to an absurd reversal of roles.

Core Idea
Independent human power would make God dependent on human cooperation.

Maturidi continues his refutation of dualism by exposing the logical consequences of claiming humans have independent power. Such a claim, he argues, would allow humans to nullify God's governance and even place God in their debt. This passage lays out the reductio ad absurdum that shows why only God has ultimate power.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Notice the conditional logic: 'if humans had power, then...'
The passage is a single argument; let the language sink in.
2
Identify the hypothetical consequence
Find the first consequence: humans could nullify the governance of the world. Then see how Maturidi extends this to messengers and each person.
3
Understand the underlying assumption
The argument is built on the idea that if humans have independent power, God cannot compel them. Maturidi shows this undermines God's authority.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Reflect on the final verdict
Maturidi calls this 'the most awful statement.' Realize that this shows the necessity of denying independent human power to preserve tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى قول هؤلاء يكون للبشر قدرة نقض تدبير العالم، وللرسل قوة أن لا يظهروا الله حجة في الأرض، وأن يمتنع كل منهم عن الوجه الذي عليه مضى تدبير، وهو مبنى على كون أحواله على أيدي البشر وخلق الأرض والسماء، والله تعالى لم يكن له قدرة على خلق تلك الأفعال والأحوال على أيديهم، ولهم قدرة على أن لا يفعلوا شيئا من ذلك، فإذا لهم عليه أرفع المن وأعلى النعم؛ إذ على القدرة في منع تقديره ونفاذ تدبيره فعلوا الذي به قام تدبيره وتم ملكه وسلطانه وعلى ما دبر وشاء، وذلك أوحش قول وبالله التوفيق.
And according to the statement of these (dualists), humans would have the power to nullify the governance of the world, and the messengers would have the power not to manifest God's proof on earth, and each of them could refrain from the course upon which governance proceeded. This is built upon the idea that His affairs are in the hands of humans, and the creation of the earth and sky [is in their hands?], and Allah, may He be exalted, had no power to create those actions and states through them, while they have the power not to do any of that. Then they would have upon Him the most elevated favor and the highest grace; for, in spite of their power to prevent His decree and the execution of His governance, they did that by which His governance stood and His kingdom and authority were completed, and upon what He decreed and willed. That is the most awful statement. And success is through Allah.
Source pages p. 859

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of the refutation of dualism, specifically attacking the notion that humans have independent power. Maturidi argues that if humans had such power, they could nullify God's governance of the world. Even the prophets could choose not to manifest God's proof. This would imply that God's plans depend on human will—an absurdity. Moreover, if humans refrain from action, they would be withholding favor from God, because God's kingdom would only be completed through their voluntary actions. This elevates humans above God, which is an 'awful statement'. Maturidi concludes that this is utterly repugnant.

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbir)
قدرة (qudra)
نقض (naqd)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think human free will means total independence from God.
Correction: Maturidi shows that total independence would allow humans to thwart God's plans, which is impossible; therefore human power is always subordinate to God's.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what would be a direct result if humans had independent power?
A) Humans would be more grateful to God
B) Humans could nullify God's governance
C) Humans would become prophets
D) Humans would create the earth

Key Takeaway
Attributing independent power to humans leads to the absurd conclusion that humans can thwart God's governance and put God in their debt.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever catch yourself assuming that your own will and power are independent of God, as if you could succeed without His enabling? Think of a specific decision this week—how would your perspective shift if you truly internalized Maturidi's argument that your every action depends on God's creation and permission?
?
In what area of your life do you rely most on your own ability, secretly believing that your effort is what makes things happen? What would it mean to surrender that area to God's governance, acknowledging that without His decree, your efforts are powerless?
?
Consider the weight of the statement that independent human power would put God in our debt. Have you ever felt that you were doing God a favor by worshipping or obeying Him? How does this lesson expose that feeling as an absurdity, and what can you do to replace it with humble gratitude?
